Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it by the ancients "bruise cure", and what you do for a patient who has this illness, if he has hair on his forehead, is to make three cuts equally long according to the length of the forehead; and let one of these cuts be as deep as two nails running down from above the root of the hairline, and the others two along the sides above the sinews, and beware of cutting the arteries that are above the sinews; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jaw, and each wound should be the size of three nails in length; have prepared a piece of sponge and much gauze to wipe away the blood, then apply a sharp spatulum from both sides as shown here.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and brandish all the cheek that is between the two cuts completely over the skin above the bone, then continue from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove the spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you place the instrument called "cultellaire" in the first incision, and it is very sharp on one side, and not sharp on the other, this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the blade cutting towards the buttock side of the heart, and the notched edge towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels descending to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to that which opens at the heart, and then make another cut in the middle incision up to the other edge; and then extract the blood equally, and express the leu for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put moist cloths in wine and oil and ointment, and keep abscesses from forming; on the third day remove the bandages, and apply large plaids of hot water, then treat with ointment basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	when a person frequently comes down with acute catarrh, and you see the eyes turned inward and small, and a weakening of vision, and burned papers; and the nose runs, and the discharge has an aqueous quality, and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that those materials and this catarrh do not come forth only from many veins, but also from the mucous membranes.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should instruct the patient to turn their head back, then make a great incision through the forehead, and another of lesser width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating. When the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton, and linen; then cover above with moistened wool in wine and oil, and be careful to avoid a hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with things that promote fleshing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In a manner: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colocynth, and make a plaster; and apply it to the wounds to draw out flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as barley, beans, peas; or flowing things such as water and fat and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear a stone or some other kind of thing that does not stick to the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it drips any amount of violet oil or sinew oil, then proceed with its extraction; and cause the patient to sneeze by means of incense, and plug the nose with ointment when sneezing comes, and place pieces of cloth or wool in the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes a sneeze from this treatment; and if it does not come, proceed with the extraction using fine forceps, of which the form is described.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it sneezes with the forceps, that is good; if not, proceed with the extraction using a fine hook of small curvature; and if it does not sneeze with this, make an ear pick from silk thread and insert the tip of the thread or a hole in the ear firmly, and plug what is around the thread with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the thread; then pull strongly to induce a sneeze, for often a sneeze comes as we have said; and if it does not come in such a manner, take glutinous resin and spread it over the stone or whatever it is, and place an instrument well prepared for this at hand, and put a little cotton inside; then press the resin on the stone or whatever it is, and pull strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not burst from all these things that we have said, you must quickly cut the ear as one would an abscess that is hot and swells and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you make the first surgeon of the patient for the cephalic, and draw out the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then seat the patient in your hands and turn the ear upwards, and cut a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or flesh hangs; and let the cut be as round as the moon until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is hard and swells, administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the spatumile tenue subtil according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tongs and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear wax that falls into the ear, the patient should use nose blowing as a first aid measure, and clean the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let the patient lie on that same ear where the wax is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it comes out forcefully through that, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your soft and light twigs, and heat them slightly on fire; and put one end of the twig in the malaide's ear, and strike from another part of his foot, and stab with another stone on the stone in the ear; and do not cease doing this from stone to stone until the arrow is completely discharged, and then thus it will be completely discharged; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end of the head into the ear, and the other head against fire until the softer reed is burned; then do this with other reeds until the arrow is completely discharged, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the arrow, if it is small, like a flea and similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, administer the extraction with forceps; and this is the thing that is easier to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and treatment of distillations, and the cure does not help much, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are no apparent worms, you draw them with fine forceps, and if they do not appear, you take the wax with which they are formed.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow inside and wide outside.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the finest probe into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient feels, then gradually expand to the entire wax; do this frequently until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to come out, plug the ear with cotton wax as I have said in the case of stones; and if they do not protrude forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in extracting worms, and you will find them treated in the treatment of distillations; and you should distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, as shown here.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be it of silver or tin fine through the little holes, and over the outer part for distillation; and to press within the distillation with an iron instrument well made for this, and if you wish take the razor and envelop between the point fit cotton; then cast your eye or your juice, and what you wish of your medicines in the wick, and let the wick be in the ear; then put within the razor all the cotton, and press your hand firmly enough until the oil is distilled or movement from the ear; and smell the sick within, and let the distillations be slightly heated on fire as one distills in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppers of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by blocking of the ear due to a wound or flesh grown within the ear, and these blockages come occasionally fully formed in the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes there is only partial closure of the perforation, and the hole is clearly visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes fully formed, if one cannot see it, is of great concern for treatment in many respects, and in that case where you can see it, you should place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, then the work has all this spatillum of which this is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be warm and cutting both in front and behind completely clear, so that it does not blister the ear; if the obstruction is of flesh grown or a growth in the ear, then use fine forceps, and remove it gently, until all the flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is perfected in the ear, take a fine sharp razor and heat it slightly on fire, then place it on the earlobe.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the operation where the patient feels grieteit in the ear, pierce slightly, and ensure that you do not damage the nerves of the ear; then place a tent in the ear according to the size of the puncture, and apply marrow in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this each day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and marrow in rose water, and powder over broken vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, it must be that you remove the tent and apply another moistened tent with cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and bandage in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other dressings that stop the bleeding which are or to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the wick of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the herb that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dried. You should spread them with tongs and forceps, and cover the head with a spatula made from its roots; then place it on the eye treated with broiled vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortication, cauterize them with the thin lens cautery, and the cauteryer moves after incision; often they repaire, because no part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	many times in papers come eyes that seem gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this the illness is called "hail," and is a gathering of moisture large on the skin above and below; the operations are such: see if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; then open it wide, then burn each part lightly, then take it with tongs, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cover it without piercing a bit the skin, then do not harm the patient; and if the rupture is large, it has a seam, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply much force, for ointments will restore it quickly and induce flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel descends into the inner part of the ear towards the upper section, invert the paper, and place the gravel with tongs, pressing it from both sides; and if the paper is removed by incision, it matters not; and when the gravel is cut, wash out the eye with salty water, and cure the wound until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is contained in the membranes of the eyelids, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and does not greatly harm their eyes. They experience catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; for this reason, they lie on their faces and sleep with the damp papers that are under them, causing swelling and appearance covered by exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the shoulder with your hands and feel the joint within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity contained within the joint of each part, then put it over it; and press with your hands from both sides so that the joints are assembled within the circle; and make a slit in the middle of the moisture along a sharp trench, and let its width not be greater than the incision made on the healthy vein; and make the skin perfectly through as you see the joint; and in many dispositions, joint fluid comes from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the wound with all one piece of flannel placed between your two fingers at the edge, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread; and guard that you do not touch in the opening, that you do not come to the entire space until the eye, that you do not injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extract does not open at the beginning of the opening, widen the opening slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten flannel in oil and water, and place over the wound, and extract with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such people who grind grain and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess hot comes to the site, apply soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs other than those natural, and they become mature, these are harmful to the eyes, and cause diseases similar to accustomed tears, softening of the papers, and albugine, to such an extent that it is a cause for the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment follows four methods: by fire cautery with all kinds of fire, or by medicine in water as described in the previous chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and缝合，或由小刀处理，根据我将要说的。
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It must be that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the skin around the eye with your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, insert a needle along the thread above; and let this be on the edge of the paper or where the hair grows among these hairs, and pull the thread above all over the paper, and cut it with scissors; then make a hole under the paper, under the added hair, to the copa spatumile from the large tearer to the small; then extract the thread, and place underneath the paper a small tent of cotton and silk, then sprinkle on the paper an image of an enche, as the laurel leaf, and always it must be that the figure is according to the quantity you see to lift the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs much of the paper according to how the paper becomes softened; then make all the spatumile on the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large lacrimal gland until small; and let it be one of the cracks near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then pour an ounce at one of the two angles of the keur, then scorch all; then assemble the two lips with a stitch using a fine needle through all the thin thread of wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluous threads on the two sorcilz above any sticky things if you wish to do this; and if not, take no care of it, then leave the stitch and the threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without a stitch with drying and constraining things, for the paper revives suddenly from the wound and the assembly of them, but the stitch is weakened (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear; and in another manner: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as like the leaf of laurel as we have recounted, at three inches severed according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cover those that overlie the small forces equally according to the form which is given here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the things are not equal, take an awl or a thread, and put one thread through the figure; and place the other thread near the large artery, and the second thread near the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then withdraw your hand equally, and withdraw all the skin above which you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment; and any time the hair of the paper turns: then use what we said about the incision; but the suturing in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you turn the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and as wide as the space is; and tie at the heads of both sides where you hold the threads; then assemble one over the other delicately above what rises from the paper of the eye, and strain the two threads from the parts formed; and leave it so for some days, and the skin which was restrained will die and nerve itself out and rot, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays healing, and you need to apply force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper is lifted, and no longer will hairs grow; and this is the form of the two threads that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you take a fine needle, and insert the thread of silk thin and fine; then assemble the heads and tie one to another carefully, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange on the skin the other fine silk thread briefly, and tie the ends of the thread; then put the patient's head into your healthy hand; and keep away from the sun so that the operations be clear, for it is a delicate and small work, then insert the needle throughout the groove at the root of the added hair, and make it pierce through the parchment quickly as long as you pull over the natural hair; then draw out the hair up to the groove, and put into the groove that hair if there be one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come forth from throughout the groove with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you shall pull the chase out through all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes out from below and that you see it with the vision of the eye; then you shall pull the chase and the thread, and close the wound for two or three days, until the hairs grow in their place and flesh arises above; and if the hairs are small, you shall accompany one long hair of natural hair, and lift it along with that or leave it, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "alecrati" or corruption, comes into the oil, it does so in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or a surgical cut, or by similar means.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put within tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not meet that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first; but use works of things that soften, such as fenugreek; and the rinse with water or decocted linen seed, and unguents melted in any oil, and wrap it in a tent, and treat it with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal completely according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are nothing other than directions for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "acracie", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds, splits, and fire cautery, and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you take a needle with a double thread, insert it into the flesh, and make a piercing from left to right so that the threads come out at both heads of the flesh; then the flesh is above all the needle, and the cloth at the spatumile large.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should, that is good; but if not, take papyrus and place it in the fissure, and turn the paper, making two fissures or cuts within the paper; and let the heads of the two fissures be at the angles of the incision you have made, and make angles such that when they are assembled, the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are agape from, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts with threads of linen; then apply the cure of those medicines we have said, of bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a full fissure beneath the hairs of the papyrus, and according to what is said above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form. The master surgeons devise means with all their power how they may make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what needs to be done and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing occurs in a human hand in such a manner that the paper above is hardened with the white of an egg and cannot move or perform its natural work, then you must insert the point of a razor beneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with tongs until you cut what is airy at the fine spatumile, which should not be too sharp or too cutting so that the patient does not suffer from the spatumile being too sharp and bleaching the eye; and your incision, in which you burnish the assembled area lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all of this is healed, and there is no scarring in an aiguate-salée (saltwater) or colère (anger) eye; then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put on the eye a moistened wool cloth soaked in abundant egg; and after three days use bandages and other soothing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail of the eye is according to two manners: it is nervous and resembling hard skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles white moist matter congealed, such that when one touches it with iron and tends it apart with forceps, one cannot hold it; and both resemble beginning near the large lacrimal gland, and grow little by little until they cover all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient places their head on your lap, then you close their eyes; lift the paper with your hand, then clamp the nail with small forceps and hold it above; then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or goat's hair, or ox's hair, and strong thread; double the tip of the needle slightly and pierce through the nail completely, securing the nail with a thread and holding it above, then scrape along the side of the nail which contains the prunelle and silk to the root of the lacrimal gland with all fine forces, leaving the natural skin or lacrimal gland, so that no tears arise in the incision as usual; sometimes clamp the nail only at the oncine and with the thread, as we have said; then scrape along the entire fine edge which forms the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the spatule does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; after incision, pour a little ground salt into the eye, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it until another day; then treat with what is needed until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the lancets cannot enter, often this semblance of a nail is treated with medicines; it heals as I have described in the division, and if you see it copulate, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatule slightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And refine the nail delicately from above, and if you see that it diminishes slightly and the reason presses in, distill into the eye a collar of litharge and a red collar and salt ground, and stop up the eye until another day; then restart the other work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as with a hot abscess, then let it alone, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the gland causes great harm to the eye, suspend it with a needle, and excise part but not all, so that no more tears arise; then instill in the eye red distillate made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises near the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's eyes once produce red flesh, which covers the pupil and is held on paper and turned upside down, seeming like a water-lily; and the work is such that the patient places his head in your direction, then you move the eyes, and all that flesh is excised with suitable needles and held by force. Then remove the first layer of flesh, cutting it down to the surface gradually until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the work; and for the incision of the spatumile, as we said in the incision of the nail and with small forces from which one removes the sebel, as the form shows after this chapter. And when the incision is completed and all flesh removed, apply brine oil or distill red colloid and similar corrosive medicines, placing a sponge soaked in egg white over the eye to ensure it remains hot; if nothing remains and the abscess does not rise, and you doubt it is a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with things that pacify a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do for any flesh that is added to the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But still it must be that you adjust the treatment for each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins around the eyes are red and cover the eye, they tolerate the work for vision and weaken the eye throughout the day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, for the first step, you must examine whether the eye is red and if it is, determine that there is no other disease except the redness; then proceed as follows: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy hand, then suspend those veins for one-tenth of an ounce according to your wisdom, and let the ounces be twice as fine in this manner:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two ounces per degree in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, having identified those veins subtly, wipe the blood hour after hour until you see the veins remove themselves from the eye; and guard that you do not damage the eye with the points of the spatumiles, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be most fervent in your work so that you do not harm any vein; and when you have done this, distill colriere green and red into the eye to corrupt what remains of the swelling.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to coil all of those in that hour, apply a poultice to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured of the warm abscess, then resume according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They are called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and medicine using hot aqueous substances as I have previously said, and if it is not healed, then you cut into the abscess, where it should come to an end, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then scrape out with all the instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "aspre chief," and be made of iron to fit the shape of the head, and be pointed like a rasp as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the bone of the corrupted area, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know that the corruption has stopped; do this once, then restore the layer of medicinal powders.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed and flesh arises, and the core of the bone is closed, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not change or become an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if this is not the case, there is another method to bring the fistula back to the perforation of the neck according to this form: and you must uncover the bone a second time with a铁，和药物浸泡，当它揭开后，取一根木棍按此形状，铁钉应有三个角，木棍应该削尖至你所见的样子。
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	place it on the delated bone of the shoulder, and keep your hand away from the eye a little, then turn to all the parts until it penetrates the bone, and let the patient feel with his hand where the veins are if he keeps his hand near his nose; and then restore the head of the shoulder with medicines dry as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the bones, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely open and there is no need to disembed or reduce swelling, it is necessary to bind the patient; then heal them, then place suction cups or catgut without cutting to extract fluid. Place on the eye the ligature made of aloe, acacia, incense, and sarcocolla, and then apply pressure to the eye, and cover with bandages and cloths; the method of the cloths is that you take soft enough cloths, fold each into four parts, and place one over the other according to the amount needed by the eyes. Then apply a hard form bandage from above, and repeat the suction cups without cutting to extract fluid. Remove the suction cups and let the eye be pressed day and night; if the ligature loosens, it is necessary to tighten it much. Remove the ligature after day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not, repeat the bandaging, cloths, and ligatures and suction cups until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the tearing of woollen fabric or vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woollen fabric or vein, then opened, and comes through the papieres like the grain of resins, and is terrifying to see; then if you see it copered, the works are such that you put an needle into the root of the part below until it reaches that above, then put another needle where there be a double thread from the part of the eyelid; and make them pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cop the leaf of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around, and hold it tight, then take out the needle and set upon the eye wool moistened in abundance of egg; and let it be until the threads adhere with the vein, then cure the eye with things comforting until the wound is healed; and any time the wound is restrained by the vein through a circle of cloth around each part, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly swollen, pierce them with a sharp needle that comes from the back of the eye, and drain the moist white substance, then let them enter quickly; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" arises from the bow of the eye that assembles in the eye, seeming like water flowing down, and it is not water. The manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a suitable chair straight, then take the head between your hands from one side, and move the eyelids until you see the bow come above your eyes; then prick it, and do not let it flow out, and remove the light, and see the patient's things as they should be; and if it does not flow out, know that it is water, and if the flowing of the bow does not appear as we have said, know that it is water.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Place the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make a cut on the corneal membrane near the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the crown, as long as the bow is out; and when it has come out, distill into the eye hot watery honeyed or boiled fenugreek water or honey, then cure with other ointments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have placed the appearances of the eye's waters in the division, and those that it is appropriate to pierce; then proceed according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It must be that you place the patient between your crossed hands, away from the sunlight, and bind the healthy eye very tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if they are right-handed; then take with your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea at the thickness of a thread along that yellow part of the eye to the lower part of the tear duct, and push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand so that it pierces through the yellow part of the eye, feeling when almagda enters the empty space; and the measure of the way almagda should be is precisely the measure from the pupil to the end of the blackness; this is the cornea of the eye. You will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument where the aqueous humor is, and express it through one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the liquid flows now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a while, and if the liquid rises again by the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is well inserted and it does not rise, then extract almagda gently by turning your hand little by little; and then put a bit of silk gemme in it, remove this from his eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put something to plug the eye, such as a piece of wet wool soaked in rose oil and abundant egg, and secure it with healthy eye tissue.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, put on a warm cloth with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens to the extent that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people whose eyes are too hard, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which the form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then pour in the hardening substance as we have said; and for the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a draught to induce sleep, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and let him be free from all movements, and give light meals, and do not move his head either to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then release him in that same dark place, and test his vision, and have him show some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not fitting that you do this during the time of treatment or after incision now, but you must loosen it, because the fluid rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if abscesses arise, you release the eye before the seventh day, following the treatment for those who alleviate an abscess; and when it is pacified, you release the vision and place over its face a small cover to protect any day, and let it be attached in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and recover as it can; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made aagda pierced, which they succeeded with water, but truly I never saw one such in our land, nor did I ever read of them in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of almagda, for those who do not know them will see; and they be of lead properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the cheek below the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes cheeks with missing parts appear different. Some of these seem like scorpions with feet; and there are those where the cheek has an embedded black part, and another where the cheek has a well-colored sore.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those cheeks that are a sore and not embedded, you must seat the patient between your hands against the sun; work his nostrils, and sprinkle an ounce on those sores, and draw them out. Then cover what you can support with a fine sharp spatumile from one side, until you know that the sore is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that one cannot cope with, open it completely with all the subtle instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if without surmounts or an abscessed foot, give him the help as it should be; and if it is malign abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the flesh be removed, then pour in or sprinkle oil and vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the oil works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is cured; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh grown on the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach for cutting: then you must put a slightly thick piece of linen thread, knotted by hand, with each knot about an inch or less apart; and place the patient's head where the thread exits into its nostril as much as possible, and pull it gently until it comes out through the nostril into the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is a light matter for one who knows how to do it; then hold the end of the head that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other end that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull alternately as we are here with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the root has spoiled that flesh, then draw the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back to the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrupt all that remains of flesh; and then put into the nose a cane of plonc for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, to which one distills the eyes and medicines or plonc.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it there; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have one hand on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the cheek below the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease arises at the top of the nose which is called "telul" and grows and becomes large; when it is seen with the eye; therefore, you must cut in the beginning, and remove all of it, then place the cautery or burning medicine over it; if one delays cutting until it becomes large, one must observe whether it is hard, of runny color, or of poor sense: do not touch it with iron at all because it is an embedded abscess, for when one cuts it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is from pus contact, not of runny color, and you see that one can cut it completely, empty the patient and cut carefully without fear, and cure it thoroughly with drying and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, for in some men.
