Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then approximate the two edges with a stitch, and treat it until it heals. And if the edges are already dry on both sides, you must cauterize all parts of their edges until they heal, then approximate the two edges with a stitch, and bind them. Sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood powder, and incense powder; then place a piece of plaster of strong or another binding plaster, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is such that you assemble the wound: either with needles, as we have said in suturing the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	By hand, abscesses appear in the lips hard, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; then it must be that you turn the lips, incise on each side, and remove with forceps and apply to each part; then cover with vitriol powder after the incision, until the wound is cleansed; and then apply linen, and dry the wound until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a sore arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with tongs and cut at its root, allowing the pus or blood to flow; then place on the head vitriol powder, or other shrinking and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after incision, as often happens, cut a second time and cauterize: it will not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellowish and worm-eaten, as decay comes to the gum, and the tooth stinks; you must place the patient in your hands, and his head on your lap, and clean the teeth or the scabs until there remains nothing; and thus cleanse the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other stains until they are all removed; and if what is to be removed according to the first reason is good, it is well; but if not, begin again from the second day and the third, until you have cleaned everything; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work shows, because those who clean between the teeth have other forms than those who clean the teeth directly; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth in its pain, you must delay the treatment as much as you can, for it should not be done at all; for it is a very delicate matter so that one may have no excuse for cutting.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to undergo treatment, it must be certain that the tooth is decayed.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain afflicts the patient, and they think it is a good tooth, and have the sound tooth treated; yet all the while the pain does not depart because the bad tooth has not been extracted, for we have already found that to be the case with these patients. And when you are well certain that the tooth is decayed, it must be that you scrape around the entire tooth with a sharp implement to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it out bit by bit using fine forceps or pliers at the first sign of looseness, until it is thoroughly loosened, then secure the forceps well. And place the head of the patient on your thigh between your knees, and hold them tightly so they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and insert it gently into each part, and agitate it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, you must fill it with wads of cotton, lint, or similar; and you should gently extract it with forceps so that it does not break during extraction; and you must carefully work around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part of it, as this can cause the patient greater pain than the initial pain due to the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act as the ignorant healer does, who, through their haste and boldness, break the cavity once and do not provide what we have recounted; but they bring about great illness one time through the incision due to the roots remaining or the cavity they break, as we often wish; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the cavity with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the cavity with vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which one must adjust the teeth on first, be long-pointed and with thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting, and let them be well-made of iron, and let them have teeth to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, you must place wet cotton soaked in butter on the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the wound is healed, use pliers called "algefri," which appear like a doctor's bill; and let them be made similarly to a rasp, and these are their shapes:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out all around these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", that is, pincers, of which see the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and large so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, that is good; if not, you aid with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you aid with this instrument that has two claws, of which see the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front by the reason of the teeth, and from this instrument which seems a pair of large forceps, of which see the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be that this instrument cannot break, and know that few instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the master surgeons themselves find their instrument subtley by themselves, according to those they perform and the disease shows them, for there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of bones and if one breaks in the flesh or another bone, or rots, so it seeks the instruments that it must have, which I have said, and helps with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, remove it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with the natural order, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know whether the tooth was born after the others and is not in its proper place, and cannot be adjusted or filed: then extract it; and if it is out of alignment with the other teeth, take this instrument whose shape is as that of a small beak, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently move it day by day with your hand due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you cannot move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a small file as its shape is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file used for making needles; and gently file the tooth day by day with your hand lightly, so that it does not move until it chieces; then in the end flatten it with a plane, using any razor. If the tooth is too sharp and blanches the tongue, you must file away its sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not blanche the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth chatter due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot hold food in their mouth without dropping it, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, it is ineffective; so you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the threads be of medium thickness neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the thinner teeth, whether one or more, until you can clearly reach the other healthy tooth; then continue the wrapping until you return to the part where you started, and withdraw your hand gently and firmly, so that they do not move at all; and let your knot be close to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the head of the tooth with a needle and assemble them, and reposition between the healthy teeth, and place it so as not to irritate the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can remain, and if it loosens or the threads break, bind it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two molar teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, fresh as possible, as we have said; and one must not do this except by those who are wise and suffer, and once a form of an osseous tooth of a deer is made, one places it in the spot where the tooth is missing, and binds it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	no wound from the tongue or naturally, that one is born thus; or by accident of a stitched wound; and the works are such that you work the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hands, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knots, and it is suddenly from a wound, then use the lancet and cut wide that ligament; and take care that the incision not be too perfect, for the artery is beneath; and when you have done, raise the head with rosewater and almond oil, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen pad; and let the patient rest each night so that the poultice may heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding comes, put on the head of the wound powdered vitriol; and if the wound weeps, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other dressings until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is of a red or black or hard color, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is turning white and there is moisture, throw in a pinch, and make a small incision with a sharp spatule, and relieve it on both sides; and if the wound weeps during your work, put powdered vitriol on it until it dries up, then return to your work until you have treated all parts; then remove the flax and salt, and treat with other dressings until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes abscesses in the throat appear, which are called "godath," and properly speaking, they are the two almond glands. And when you treat them as we have said in the division, if they are hard, small in size, and of a fleshy color, be careful not to touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron at all, also for the discharge of blood; but leave them until they are healed, and then you can remove them, or they would break on their own. And if they are whitish in color and the root is fine, have prepared the instrument for cutting, but first see if the abscess has cooled and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, seat the patient facing the sun, and his head in your care, and let him close his mouth, and the sergeant hold the instrument between his hands, pressing the tongue under the entire instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be made of fine silver or brass as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And press the tongue with this instrument entirely, and you see the abscess, take an ounce and the tip in the almond, and draw force above more than you can; and do not pull anything from the threads with it, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, that resembles strong forces; and all ways the heads are bent, one next the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, use tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and the other named; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner. After the incision, gargle the patient with hot, strong water, or warm and mild water, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or cooked pomegranate peel, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then cure it as long as it is healed. And sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, so you should cut them accordingly, just as you did the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman who had an abscess that was born within her throat, that is to say, the small abscess; and I nearly closed up all of her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained in such a state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it required two fingers to be placed through the two openings of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then soon, and inserted the cautery into one opening, then withdrew it, and removed a large portion of the flesh; afterwards, I inserted the cautery into the other neck opening, and forced her mouth open and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the cautery into these abscesses, and extracted much of the pus, and only a little blood came out; thus was the passage of the throat unclogged for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting into this abscess for a long time; and the abscesses recurred, and filled the space that I had vacated until it grew very large; then I cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left those parts, and let God decide what would happen to her from then on.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum gathers in the eye, and it swells and becomes long, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is large and round, it is called "uve.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the swelling of the abscesses is alleviated and it is fine, then it is appropriate to cut it; and that which is round gathered and not long, and is either bloody or of flax color or black, it is appropriate to avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it in the manner I have said, according to its blenchor and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier. Then, insert the oncine into the eye, draw it out, and cut with the two instruments I spoke of in the incision of the two almond-shaped areas.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not apply too much heat that exceeds the natural limit; for if you apply more, it will harm the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we have said about the treatment after cutting the almonds, and continue the care until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of applying heat, you must use an instrument for the cautery to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is with hot water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head on your hand, and then press their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned or the cautery chapter. Use fresh hot water that is neither too thick nor too clear; and fill the instrument with this water, as described below:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be one hair or hole where the medicine is placed, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and muscle fluid run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the blepharitis; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for half an hour of time, until you see it infused and the bites of the medicine are pacified; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton above, so that the cotton wicks up on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the medicine for the cautery, do so, and after the cautery wash around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cleaned with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take a reed and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and violets and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in one pot, and pour oil into it, and cause it to boil; and the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and among the pot let there be the instrument wrapped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And may be of silver or iron, and may one of the heads be inserted in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the tube, until the eye is numbed; after that, renew often, until the eye dries up, and guard that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things occur; and do not do so when the hot abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the shoulder of the patient so that it does not become too hot for the patient; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and this is a good cure overall for healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens to the throat os or spiny fish bone, or some other thing; therefore, you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue with all the instrument under the sun so that you see the thing move; and what does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach; by chance it might be expelled by vomiting; or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will break open, and then you can pull out the force. And if it does not come out as we have said, take the plunger instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the probe enter the throat more easily at the head, with the head held high; and be sure not to touch the epiglottis, lest it swell or the bone be pushed in; and when the patient moves, have them blow the probe, for this will either cause them to swallow or pull it out completely with equal force.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the throat juice
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No juice of the throat is medicated as I have said in the division through the treatment with medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after you press the tongue with the probe that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, draw it off with a very small lancet, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the throat of the patient, then blow hot air from the cane, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is sick with fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and give it to swallow, moving it with his hand often; and as soon as the blood tastes the water, let him spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit out as we have said, submerge the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned in the eye fumigation; do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot which has charcoal visible in it, and let the position be covered by a perforated cover, and into that perforation put the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation in, and the patient put the end of the cane in his mouth, and close the mouth, so that the smoke does not come out but goes to the pus; and the pus will fall now, and if it does not fall, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and allow the patient thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to be forced out by this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the pus, is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tongs to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot let go. See here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	much of the similarities of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings forth in this book from one to another, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two ways of which one is in its very likeness and of that which it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those lues where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those in the body, and abscesses of fatty tissue are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses one must not perforate them until the bowels are dead according to their completion; and there are such that it is necessary to perforate them when they are ripe, even if they do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them be until they are rotten within, by chance the ligaments and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or when the abscess is within the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or if it is within the foundation, then pierce it in the same way once it is dead. It does not matter that you perforate an abscess that has no sense of digestion completed, except when that which is within the foundation may rot completely and lengthen within, and become a fistula; and cannot heal in great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating the abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and the movement and sharpening at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where the abscess depends more upon the body, and where it moves most. And let the perforation be as long as the body allows, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equally without any folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in living flesh, it is best to leave the perforation until its digestion is completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you perforate before it is fully digested, the body will be lengthened by the venom of it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance, the edges and depths may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if for any abscess that is perforated according to the size of the body, as the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must use small punctures for small abscesses and large punctures for large abscesses, as well as many cuts according to the size of the abscess. And for such abscesses where it is necessary to lance the heart and cover; when it has become hard like a flax seed and softened, you must do so as with boils: and for those that are cut into three angles, and for those from which one covers like the leaf of juniper, as with angry abscesses; and for those where a round incision is made, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Who have no head, as with a superficial abscess or carbuncle, it is necessary that you pierce them completely; and when the abscess is large, and has gathered much pus, if you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once in that hour, but only part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, and again draw something from it; do this many times, gradually, until the pus is completely gone; similarly, if the patient has weak virtue, or a woman in childbirth, or small children, or old and decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For if the patient shudders several times with the discharge of the pus, that by chance kills the patient, and you are not to blame.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware of this chapter with great caution, and when you perceive your abscess, cleanse the wound, and observe whether the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a clean cut, administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many perforations, it must be that in each one you put a tent so they come against each other; and if you have incised part of the skin and covered it over, it must be filled with old cotton or shredded linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the bleeding occurs during your work, administer cold water and ease it, and place a soft cloth over the area bleeding many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, and it is managed and treated, and the powders that I have said in this book are applied to their wounds, and if it is or seems winter, and the veins or abscesses are very nervous, then you must place wet cloths on tents and blankets soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the flesh is soft, then you must place wet cloths on blankets soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and dress and treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: for you have already been told how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	from the shoulder
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses appear on the head, and their appearance is like little bags, as with the strings of a berry, and there are many that resemble them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and such with moisture like grapes; and some are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the flank are such that you test with any instrument called "entromissoire," from which the form follows, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let it out through the top for a long time.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is removed, scar him without leaving the skin that contains that moisture, for it will repeatedly dislocate if nothing is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise, in water and salt, and apply to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and let those things that remain from the night drain.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton application as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds on to fatty matter, shape the cut according to this form, longwise; and throw in your pinchers, and cauterize from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery acts contrary, do as I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so for the abscess if it is stony, and for cutting and treating as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when you cut into the stony abscess and the moisture, it is less dangerous, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and among those I treated were abscesses from an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a smooth, rough, and white stone, and could not be broken; and if any had been cut open, it would have resulted in a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or heads, those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest part, so that the pus can exit; and treat them as they should be treated.
des scrophules	of the scrofulous swellings
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times such an abscess occurs in the neck, beneath the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes comes from other parts or organs, and are hard, and are joined together with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous swelling is properly within its own region, like the knot and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulous swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some contain moisture, and some are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good condition upon touch, and resemble the color of the skin, move in all parts and are not eroded near the neck nor the artery nor the vein, and are not deep; it is necessary that you scrape from above, and burn each part, sew the two lips of the wound with needles if needed, as we have said for abscesses of the head. Drain a little at a time, and be sure that you do not damage the nerve or the vein, nor the spinal fluid nor the cutting nerves, lest your hand slip and go too far, so that you do not scrape what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you pierce the vein or the artery, and it does not allow you to continue, put vitriol powder or any other powders that stop bleeding into the wound, and hold the wound; and let it be until the abscesses are pacified, and the wound softens and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stopped bleeding, return to your work until you complete it; then rest according to your proper indication if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, treat and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not fitting that you pierce that swelling at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound, and suture them now, since there has been no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cut the root of it, and extract it forcefully, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that have excess, pierce it where it opens naturally; and pierce it as was said before, depending on the location, then apply lint with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, continue the treatment with ointments promoting healing until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrophula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have scrophula, it is necessary that the cutting of the throat which is called "epiglote" be performed; and one should not seek help through this, because all the veins and the tumour in the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the jugular vein, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It must therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, be cut over three or four small cuts through, between the two circles or by the size of the cut as from the skin, and not in the cartilage; and those thus are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched from the entire inch of the throat, then cut the vein until it comes to the thread; and avoid the vessels of blood if you see any thing, and then cope the skin as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the fluid of the thread which leaps forth through the broken part, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which strangulation is doubted, bring together the two edges of the wound in the heart, and suture it well over the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim said that one should not do this until the throat is completely numbed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and then the defect is addressed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from dying; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passes, and it passes in three or four days. Then they commanded to suture and treat the wound until it heals; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; and I was called to perform the cure, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood issuing from it. I knew that she had not pierced a vein or artery, but the windpipe was injured by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened,缝合了伤口，并尽我所能治愈她； maiden did not suffer from hoarseness, and recovered her voice; for this reason, I say that in the treatment of the epiglottis there is no cause for fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the main windpipe
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like that of a hazel, and it is very common in women; and it occurs according to two manners: natural and accident; or naturally it has no artifice.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two manners, of which one is similar to fatty lumps, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from within the artery; and there is fear, and it should not be treated by making openings except in that which is small, and prove and search through all the intervening areas: if you find it as fatty and cannot be distinguished from a vein, cut it out as one cuts fatty lumps, and draw it to its head if there is any; and seek quickly, and cure it as it should be until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many methods we have, of which I will speak all the similarities; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference there is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever lasting until the boiling has passed, and putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	When the issue has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the syphacia, which is its own sac and according to the color of the body, it begins like a sore and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, or grease, or moisture, and much of its color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses and new wounds is that you probe or more moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn thy two poles little by little, until thou knowest that the instruments have reached the core; then do it according to the size of the abscess; then extract the entromissoire, and take care in this that if it should fail.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes out clear or of any color, cut it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire no moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, so cut it crosswise, and take it with forceps, and burn gently from each side. Guard the spot where it lies, and treat it soundly with the wound. And if you cannot treat it soundly, cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is nothing left, it returns to us many times; and if there remains a little, and the pus grieves, fill the wound with some corrosive powders, bind the wound, and place warm abscess-pacifying things on it until it heals; and if the wound is large, suture the two edges of the wound, and treat as those who attend to flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beating is contrary to you or some other thing hastens it, use the juice of vitriol powdered, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood; then return to the copper that has remained from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the interruptive instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small. Among them are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb." These too are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses from fistulae; and they are like the needles used for stitches, made of yellow brass or iron or silver, with those that are yellow being more effective than black ones for encircling corruptions from fistulae. They come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the oncin are of similar semblances, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and among these, there are oncin with two corners in three manners also; and among them, there are oncin with three corners, and they are of three manners also; and among them, there are oncin with two corners, and oncin with only one corner, and they are of three manners; and all of this are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these that one makes is sharp, and among them are those that cut only half-way, for which one cauterizes the nostrils, because one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and from these intruments are the alemeles placed in palms, so that the patient does not perceive at the opening of abscesses; and they are of three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses none but in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, mamels, and in similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling shells of almonds, according to this form, for which one stops the bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once in its place which heals by copulation of veins and arteries, and again they do so according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to腐烂，直到看起来像女人的乳房；并且留着难看且肿胀的状态，看到需要治疗的人应根据这一行的规定进行处理 .b. 到 .g.：
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then cauterize the fat, and apply medicine to the wound with astringent properties, then suture the two edges of the wound, and treat until it heals; and if the breast hangs down and becomes soft due to its size as in women, cut into the rib above, by similar incisions; so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the menses according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then cauterize the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and administer what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not entirely complete, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the corruption of blood, it is necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it eats away the remaining flesh and fat, then treat until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of arrow wounds
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from arrow wounds are like hardened scrofula, or have lumps, and if they contain moisture, they do.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said for cuts in scrofula, and if the wound contains bowe, apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn shut, many abscesses often occur; similarly, it happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. If one recognizes this due to the artery, the abscesses are long and well-formed; and when you feel it with your hand, you sense the constriction; and when it is due to the vein, it appears as swelling and a pulsation; and it is foolish to attempt to treat such an abscess, especially when it is under the armpits, at the groin, or near the neck and many other places, and is very large.
