Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one should avoid the iron cure. For those in chief, it is also advisable to avoid it. In the case of swelling from an artery, make a cut through the skin longwise; then operate on the size with pins, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle under it, and pierce it all the way to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in extracting the two arteries in the temples; then move the skin between the two threads so that what is inside comes out, and thus separate the abscess; then administer the cure according to bowe's method until the threads dissolve; afterwards, apply ointment suitable for this condition until it heals; if the abscess is due to the swelling of a vein, you should dye your hand with as much of the abscess as possible onto the skin, then insert the needle under the thread you hold in your hand and pierce it, keeping the double thread so that it passes through to the other side; then tie the abscess as I have said, or bind one part of the threads around both shoulders; if you doubt whether the threads are secure, take another needle and pierce all over the abscess from the incision of the first needle, holding the threads in three places; then drain the abscess until the excess comes out, then drain the excess from the skin and leave what is tied; finally, place a moist cloth on vinegar and oil, and continue with bandages and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses coming to the artery and vein, abscesses of the nerves when they are injured, or through too great exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more frequently in joints and in all places where there are joints, and it is the grief of abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when one restrains it forcefully, the patient feels great pain, and not just from the flesh, but beneath the heart; and it moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither below nor above, and that which is in joints should not be treated with iron: by chance it might cause contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead cuts through the skin to the bone.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and lance at its base; and if it is large, suspend it by a thread, cauterize it, then extract it and suture the wound, and continue the treatment until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	If the large boils are hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it occurs in the belly and nowhere else; it is a disease called "fungus" by similarity to mushrooms, and it has fine roots and large heads. In them there are both small and very large ones. I have seen men who had two bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, and they were white, had fine roots, and were split in half, and in them always remains moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI drachms, and the work in incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of fine root; so you cop it at the spatillum large, and let the cautery be at fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in sawing there often come great hemorrhages, and if the vein breaks, then you must hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient fainting and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made plucking thread, and place it on the artelul as we have said, and let it be for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the plucking thread until it copes the artelul, and work each by itself; and if the roots are large, you must fear to cope immediately for the belly, but you may well cope half of it, then cauterize that it not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cope the thule which is of fugue color and of poor sense and let regart.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an embedded abscess, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a fire cautery on a wound or a cut in the skin, and is on the abdomen with some of the boils, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from windiness; and if it is by the rupture of the skin and the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and is a light thing without pain, and obvious from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestines, then it is more varied, and when pressed at its base, it rises and then returns, and sometimes becomes swollen, and greatly increases at the entry to the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and clearly apparent when you press with your hand; it does not constrain. And if it is due to blood, it is clearly shown by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are placed according to quantity; and if it is due to pneuma, it is swollen upon touch, and the work is that you look to see whether the appearance is of arterial or venous blood, or pneuma.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then you must let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the boil, then you must instruct the patient to extend his arm, and stretch it fully out straight; then pierce all around the armpit; then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go around the limb that you have pierced with all the spatumile, then place half of the abscess above at the large uncine; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk, and let it be fastened well; then work on the other half of the abscess extended over the thread, and use your index finger to press the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, release it, and return the intestine to its place in the abdomen; and if you find the boil, take it with the uncine and drain the excess; and if the artery acts contrary or the vein, go right through, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads, and insert the needles into the cross that you made by piercing; then extract the abscess in four parts over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb until it rots, and bury the dead flesh on its own; or you drain it when it is fine and rotten, then treat the limb as needed, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the limb as needed, and suture the limb.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the signs of chancre, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one should avoid the iron cure; and we say that chancres arise in the groin, and great caution is needed in the treatment. The ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped away, as those on the sameles, thigh, and similar places, you must remove them all when they are at the beginning; but when they are large and old, it is not fitting to approach them, for I have never seen any healed by this method, nor has anyone been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him sanious if he has evident fullness, then prepare the patient well by letting him lie on his back for the operation; then throw out the tumor or chancre, and all the hair from all parts, removing everything without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, hold the place well in your hand or with some object, and if the hemorrhage contradicts the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then treat with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken of the symptoms of dropsy, and how the assembly of the water is made, and the signs of each symptom, and the cure through medicines, and that cured by iron: it is only clarified; and one must not use iron in these two symptoms: namely, tympanites and yposarche, because they are deadly things; therefore, when you treat this symptom of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not help, see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as an immediate solution of the belly and similar things; then do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient in good health, and he only has dropsy, and is neither too thin nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the attendants press the belly by directing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the spatumile thorn according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	A point, and in any way let it not be too deep that it can come as far as the intestines when inserted, and cannot be withdrawn; then see if the hydrocele is near the intestines: so you must cut underneath the scrotum three incisions directly over the knife. And if the hydrocele is due to liver disease, so let your incision be on the left side of the scrotum three incisions; and if it is due to the mesentery, so let it be on the right, and it must not be that the patient lies with the incision such that the superfluities do not flow to that weak side; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push out, and lift your hand away from all the serous fluid between the skin and the surface as if scraping in quantity of a nail or a little more. Then pierce the surface until the serous fluid comes to the right place, and these are the outlets for the water, then remove the instrument with the form given here:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver pin, and it is made of light brass or iron, and it is placed below the small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	On the head above is the alemele, such that when the instrument comes to the edge, it should be placed slightly above the instrument now; fill it then with half or a third part, for if you empty more than necessary in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he may faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and hold the edge, and it is held now for the key which stops the hole which is above the syphax, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then repeat the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw a small quantity of fluid; do this any day, and beware of following too much until it remains but a little fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water in him, cure with warm earth or sand, and by much sweating or bath and in the sun, and let him drink; cure with medicines desiccative until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have pores in the penis, or the pores are small, or they are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to act quickly before the semen becomes very subtle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or pierce a small hole in the plonc, and seal it and keep it thus for 3 or 4 days, and when it is ready to urinate, remove the plug, and allow urination, then replace it; and by chance it may not be necessary, for the urine that comes forth does not leave the plug closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the hole is small, it should be treated with a plug of plonc, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in their place are bledder, for none are born with the hole at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the gland, and this is a bad illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then the head of the verge and the cope are made as the size of a feather's shaft, so that the punctures are made in the middle, as it should; and beware of the outflow of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these sores come in the verge, and they are an appearance of foul flesh; and among them there are both benign and malignant; so you must treat them with a sharp lancet, cut and cleanse all of them, then place soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure them with diafinicon ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and foul-smelling, you must apply a fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when you have excised it, and if the ulcer is in the verge, and has part within the skin and part without, you must first remove the ulcer that is within; and when it is dressed, treat it without.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you dress it all together, it is not assured that the head of the verge will not be pierced, and black corruption comes into the verge and where it coagulates; you must cut out all that is black and corrupted, then bind with a plaster made of apple peel and flour from pomegranate seeds, then dress with other plasters until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids in two dispositions together: namely, in bleeding and in corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you must insert a string of flax into the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair grows at the head of the penis that affects those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then you must therefore cauterize with a heated instrument just enough to loosen the ligaments, freeing the head of the penis from all sides; and if it is a serious matter to describe this, then you must cauterize with a spatulum for a small part at the head of the penis and the skin; then separate well between them, and apply a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that the hair does not grow again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work of our will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the most gentle for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have none but what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision using dilators, forceps, and with an entire pair of pincers; they found it difficult because there are two blades, and by accident one might close the upper one while the lower remains open.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is hindered by copper, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is from below, the points of the limb are not assured; and in the purification of the nail, by accident the iron escapes, and work runs amok, and many times they arise thus without needing purification and I have seen it so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the purification which is done with forceps on all the strand of hair, I have found the virtue of the experiment, for the forceps cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally on all strands of hair; but that the hairs be very thin under the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he hears it, that you only slightly tie the hair around the shaft, and let him see it in every possible way; then hold it straight between your hands, and place the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow or kiss, and draw it up as high as the head of the shaft is in; then purify well from the filth that has gathered, then tie the root with a double thread, then tie under strand by strand; and hold it at two dohs by the second hour in pocket and on the index finger, and copulate between the two ties, then lift the keur hastily and draw the head of the shaft; then let the blood flow little by little, for it is the mudder; and sprinkle powder there and over the powder attach a moistened half of a hard-boiled egg with rose water, confected with rose oil well and fresh, and leave it on until another day, and cure from other cures until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forceps for reduction is as follows: the two heads should be tight and sharp, and the heads of the shoulders should be as large as the fingers are equal.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in reduction is when the heads inside come out at the incision; therefore, you must spread them with your finger, just as the fingers make an abscess; and hold them evenly, and if you cannot hold them with your finger, hold them with forceps, and then spread them.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they penetrate for three days, and that which is beneath the scrotum is swollen, let it be left until the abscesses are calmed, and gently scar them; hold them as you can move, and take care not to touch the part of the scrotum, as this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the head of the sore wound with powder things, as we have said in treating powders, and if one copes too much from the heart, and it goes above, it will not harm; cure it therefore, as we have said, until it be healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retainment of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or congealed blood, or bowels, or new flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division. And if the urine is not relieved and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in or near the neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to bend his knees; and weights should be placed on the back, and he should extend his belly above the back, and restrain the patient as much as he can. Thus, the necks of the bladder are constrained to allow the passage of the stone above, so that the urine is relieved. And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, it is necessary for you to administer an extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which here is the form: and it should be made of fine silver, light and thin like a bird's feather; and the tube should be one and a half palm long, and very thin at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take a double thread, and tie at its end a little wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut off the excess of the wool and fill it up to the head of the syringe; then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on the seat, and rub his bladder and penis with wet oil and olive oil and water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it comes to the root of the penis, then cover the penis from above towards the mouth; then fill the syringe before up to the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine coming to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because the conductor where it goes is twisted; then draw out the thread little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make the urine flow; and continue with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and bind up the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is present, and you see it discharge acidic fluids and medications, then use an instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you can see; the leaves are fixed in place so that the medicines come out clearly, ensuring they anesthetize well the urethra. Thus, when moisture needs to be removed or added, place the head of the tube in the moisture and pull out the tube slowly; by pulling the tube out, you remove the moisture from it, and then push it back in forcefully; this way, the moisture enters and reaches the bladder, allowing the patient to feel its effects. This is the form of the fine catheter used to treat the bladder: as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or steel, and the head is higher; and below on the chest where the threads fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you see to moisten the bladder, then tie between the two breasts forming a single double thread, and heat that bit of moisture over the fire; then insert the tip of the catheter into the urethra, then draw your hand on the bladder until all the moisture is applied appropriately, so that the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce roundly through it; then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the frame, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture flows to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already discussed in the division the ways of stone, and their extraction along with medicines; and we have said the difference between a stone in the bladder and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate for its size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine has left the bladder seeming like urine in its subtlety; and it openly hardens, and grieves the patient's vein, and pierces many times, and then grows rigid; and most of these jumps are fundamental; and the cure is light for children until they are four years old, and is very grievous in the elderly, and is intermediate for those between childhood and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it must first be cleansed by enema to draw all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs at times in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and unbend and move them out of place, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and exits once from above; then have him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder hangs entirely downward; then hold it and touch it internally; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to incise over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall on touching from above, soften your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is fat, or your middle finger, if the patient is thin; then bend inwards and hold the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pinch at the neck of the bladder; then press near your finger and incise where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend the thorns in his right hand upwards, and remove the skin which is beneath the thorns in the part where the incision is made; then pour in the spatumile copant, of which this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what is between the thorns and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left navel; and be straight above the stone, and your two hands should be near the fundament, and make the incision through so that it is wide on the outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, pressing hard where your hand is at the fundament, she may burst without effort; and know that there are stones with angles and margins: they are easier to remove; and some are under, resembling a glans and round, from which the release is gentle.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not open, you must clamp with pincers that are as sharp as a file on the head, to draw the stone so that it does not escape; or you insert under the instrument a thin curved probe into the head; and if you cannot manage this way, widen the hole slightly, and if it is uncoursed, draw it out with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first insert the larger one at the neck of the bladder, then cover up, then pull forcefully, and the smaller ones afterward if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must sew it up, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through it so that the wounds cannot be sutured; but nonetheless, you must strive to treat it or dismember with pincers until you sew it in pieces. When you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and draw it, and place a moist cloth covered in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then rebandage the patient on the third day, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, arise much well the place of oil and water, then treat with ointment of deflacion and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses, corrosion, and coagulation of blood in the bladder cause urine retention, which is known to occur in such a manner that it moves with the urine: pour therefore your thumb into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder; then wash the wound with water and oil and salt, and aid it in all ways until it is healed; and you must bind both thighs whenever you treat it, and apply the medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra, and urine cannot pass; you should cut as I said before, many times, and this cutting due to the treatment is excused.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take three iron forks according to this form and fix them in the coals:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the fork gently into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork in the stone little by little, as much as you can pierce the stone from another side; urine will come forth soon, then press your hand above what remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken soon, and urinates with it, the patient recovers. And if you cannot do this for any reason, tie a thread under the stone and another above, then make a cut next to the stone between the two threads, extract it, untie one of the threads, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When a stone becomes incarcerated in women, and if it happens even once, the patient should be treated carefully, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who will reveal herself to the mirrors, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stones of the woman are more imperfect than those of the man, which is why it requires a deeper incision, and great fear arises. And if necessity demands this from you, then you must seek a midwife well knowing, and often find her among the women. If you do not find one, you may resort to a very subtle instrument; and present a safe woman in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to perform what you command concerning the inquiry of the stone; and closely observe if the woman is a virgin: then she must place her foundation or base and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain her under her foundation, and recommend that she place her foundation or in the patient, and feel and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it must be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then incise on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, let that part appear, and feel the stone in that area; do not move your hand over or under the stone, and make the cut first small; then insert the forceps into the cut, if you feel the stone increase the wound until the stone can exit fully, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with grooves.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone wanes, put vitriol in its place and keep it there for an hour until the stone is extinguished; then return to your work as long as the stone remains. Have with you the instruments I said for the extraction of stones when helping you with your task. And if the stone wanes, and this is from the artery that has been incised, put powder on its place and use linen and bandages, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone alone and do not treat it further, lest by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the strength returns, then return to your work until the stones are healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous humor is nothing but a collection of moisture or white fluid, which comes from the heart of the yolk, containing the egg; and it is called "syphac" and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg if one thinks it is another egg. And it is the skin of the yolk between the white fluid we have said; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this fluid is due to weakness that comes from the yolk, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it is a color inclining to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is as white as we have said, it is an abscess, just barely long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, for it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper membrane, it is an abscess with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joint and the white as it should be, then one feels it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you prove it by introducing a square probe, of which the form is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introductory part, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cauterize with iron, the patient must be bled according to our power and the filling of his body; then place the sponge on his back, on one thing somewhat high, and put much wool under him; sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart; then take the clean spatheum and scrape the skin between them long until close to the edge of the knife, and make a straight cut in the skin of the ribs up to the white, and burn it subtly according to our power; then puncture the white full of water with large holes, and drain all the water, and then put on the pins, and elevate the white; and do not touch the heart of the ribs, but only the white; cut all or in pieces exactly the side of him subtly, that if you do not scrape well, the water will return; and if the egg has failed in your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white; then sew the two flaps of the heart of the ribs with a seam, and cure it as other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it must be that you bind the vessels that are suspensive, doubting the outflow of blood; then cut around the entire suspensive area, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if an abscess is gathered into two parts joined together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, afterwards wipe away the blood, and put in the wound moistened wool in rose oil; and place another moistened wool in wine and oil, and set above the two incisions, and cover with doubled cloth, and bind it all according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fold them with torn wool according to this likeness, and sew them together at the waist of the breeches. One head of the shoulder is placed from behind up to the back, and the other to the part below the armpit; and the other two heads above the two angles, and all the binding is gathered in the loop of the breeches; and this branch is often treated with a fire cautery instead of iron branding, and you should take the sharp cautery needle, and incise the skin at the points, and sear it with this hot sharp cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cope in all manners that you can, until you dry all out; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more saved; and use guarding against the flow of blood, and know the works of cutting; and if nothing makes thee contrary, or abscesses, or flows of blood, or other things, so cure what makes thee contrary, according to those who are before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, then administer perforation as I have said. This is when you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that an abscessed lump is present, so make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part, making the incision wide and long along the length of the body; let the openings be large so that all the fluid can drain out. Then place cotton over the area and tie it, allowing the remaining fluid to drain, and continue to treat until the wound heals. If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit through the opening in the wound, then you must insert a pin or the instrument used for draining dropsy fluids, as described before; widen the hole in the wound, and know that the fluid will return and gather after about six months or so. When it has gathered as described before, then the patient's days will pass peacefully.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess at its base
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In this section of the branch there is fear in many dispositions, which makes it seem to me that movement would be better if we leave it alone; and I will tell you the work and similar things regarding the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from wounds, and especially from the shoulders; and this happens by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to say that abscesses come from excess of sour and cold humor, which spreads to the shoulders, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the body; and it does not find any pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by chance it may be painful and stony abscesses, with fugitive color, and sometimes comes from an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the arrangement of the hot abscess, when you press with your thumb; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	That which is caused by venous swelling is known by its arrangement upon touch with the thumbs, and can well be cut from this appearance and from other marks; and you must turn the heart of the cord upwards, and make the thread of the white firm, and release the suspender from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already seated with these marks, then you must incise the egg and the cord; and if it is firm at the bottom or within the vessels, then you must release all the vein completely, and roundly cut the cord.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birthplace of the flesh is open behind, it must be cut entirely, and the egg extracted as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is accomplished, dress the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other salves until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the thigh
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a borjon, with the thigh softened. The patient moves painfully; and the treatment for this disease is well prepared similarly to the one mentioned before, and we will detail the work of it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It must be that you seat the patient on an elevated chair, then place the suspensory ligament of the testicles below your knees, at all the vessels near the groin, and tie them tightly and extend them; then cut with a sharp spatula along the path through the vessels until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each part as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a needle where it has the double thread, and attach it to the first place where the vein came, and again attach it to the other end; then bandage in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures; then treat the wound as with others where fluid is drained, so that no vessel breaks that nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there comes no harm, and if it happens in all the vessels that veins break, it must be that you take out the veins from all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the tendon
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this injury occur through sectioning that comes from the tendon or from extension in the abdomen in the part of the inguinal region, for which reason the intestines descend due to that rupture to one of the groins; and this rupture is either from the tendon or from its extension, and come about in two manners of causes: from percussion, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy load, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the tendon are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until near the surface, because the tendon presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the tendon, which causes an sudden onset of pain, and the abscesses appear varied and beneath the skin, because of the discharge of the intestines and the core below the tendon.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the circles with the intestines, and are retained within, and cause great suffering to the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron, for which it is advisable to avoid.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of this work is that you command or instruct the patient to remove the intestines with his hand inside the wound if they can enter; then wrap them around his neck, and lieve the thighs; then place the keur above, and scrape all the skin from the long coions; then insert the leivers of the tail uncines according to what you need to open the wound, and let them be such that the oes could issue forth; then scar the syface that is beneath the skin of the coions, until the white syface is uncovered on all sides; then place your index finger in what follows the coion, between the white syface which is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second syface, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second syface; and then move with your right hand inside the keur of the coions, and let the white syface be on top with your left hand, and lieve the egg towards the tail; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and release what is behind the ligament;
