and rest your fingers if there is any intestine enveloped or hard white syface, and if you find anything of this sort, put it back into the belly beneath; then take an awl with a thick thread made of ten threads, and place it in the rear part of the syface, which is after the skin of the coions; behind the tail, then scrape off the heads that appear from the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and attach the syface, which we said is beneath the skin of the coions, with a strong thread of two parts; then wrap the heads of the threads, and tie firmly with two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter out, that the abscess may not come again; and place the thread according to the first long thread over two fingers, and after these two threads leave the syface which is beneath the keur of the coions the size of a finger's breadth; then according to the roundness that the egg carries; then scrape in the part which is beneath the skin of the coions, as we have said before; then apply moistened wool, and put it on the wounds, and give the thread as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites of the eyes are cauterized to prevent excessive bleeding after incision due to doubt.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the thread until it falls by itself; and if it delays in falling, so soak it in hot water, and apply what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with other dressings until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never known anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the wire that is twisted together into a vis, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after lightly incising them. Then cut it open in half, and treat the abscess as one who works on it until the vessels constrict; and continue to treat it as we have said until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes there is a rupture in the veins, as we have said, and it becomes apparent; and no parts of the intestines are revealed at the incision, and if any do reveal, it is little, and heals every hour; and yet if it remains too long in this point, the wound or syphax forms because the intestines do reveal; and this happens due to the extension of the syphax which is in the veins, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swollen the veins and become apparent; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes the wound is cured by a iron in this manner: and that is when the patient lies prone on their back between your hands, then cut out the vein from the large swelling according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the syphax which is under the skin that ensues, then take the rag and place it over the apparent vein; and press it thoroughly over the abdomen, then suture the two veins appearing over the head of the rag, and suture one and the other; then extract the head of the rag, and neither cover the syphax nor extend the swelling or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure it by the method of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and shows no sign in the rupture, and the cauteries are moistened in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin around the knees
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin around the knees is softened in some individuals, because the flesh within is softened, and it can be seen; and when one wishes to treat it, the patient should lie on their back, and the soft skin is cut away from the natural skin. Then the two edges are sewn together with one stitch, and if necessary, the excess soft skin should be sown with three or four stitches firmly. After sewing between the stitches, the wound should be treated as other wounds until it heals, and then cut the thread.
dou chastrement	by due chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	By due chastisement is esteemed in our law, and for this reason it pleases me that I not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary for two reasons: one, that the eyes know how to answer when asked about it and know its treatment; and the other, because we often have need to chastise some beasts to aid us, as with goats, sheep, dogs, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that chastisement is done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we do by attraction, place the beast in hot water until the joints become soft and remain so. Then grasp them with your hand while they are still flexible and you no longer feel resistance.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castrating the tail: You must dye the beast, and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut each testicle one by one when you have well scorched them; and leave a little bit of the thick fat which is under the vessels; and this way of castration is better than that made by suction, because in suction something from the scrotum remains by chance, which causes the beast to desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles it appears as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in them urination occurs.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, and it is done with a knife as with a rod and two fingers.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of the man and woman is that you clean all the wounds thoroughly, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urine leaks through the skin of the fingers, there is no need to treat.
de la tentigene	of the wart
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wart is a wound that has displaced on the natural part, to the extent that it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is how they are treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must dye the excess of the wart with your hand or fingers and clean it lightly; and do not perfume it too much, so that no bleeding occurs. Then treat it with other treatments until it heals. And for a wound that arises at the mouth of the vein, cover it and perhaps it will heal on its own, resembling the shape of a cow, which is why the ancients called it the "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to apply it, as we have said regarding the texture and treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	If it is necessary to apply it, as we have said regarding the texture and treatment until it is healed.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not known, or the perforation is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident caused by illness that came about; or it is due to a foreign body, or a thick or thin fluid, and is made perfect in the thighs, or flanks, or below, or anywhere; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and sometimes the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is through the sight of the midwife.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swellings are nearby and apparent, feel with your fingers or touch them.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a thin blister and it is near the two flanks, hasten, and treat it thus: bring your two thumbs together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two flaps, so that the thin blister may be removed, and over the stumps; then take wool, and fat in oil, and place it on the wound, and lie with the woman each day, so that it does not heal over.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the blister is hard and thick, it is necessary to cut it with a scalpel resembling a bay leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stumps are of new flesh, suspend them with a needle and thread; and have the止血药物, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, incense, and plenty of egg yolk; then apply a broad bandage, so that the wound does not heal over; and thus keep it long. Then give him linen bandages until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when carbuncles bring forth pus, one must treat it according to this manner, unless it is an embedded abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the embedded abscess in the carbuncle, one must not touch it to incise.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are dilatations of veins that, without intervention, often occur. And when hemorrhoids are old, they become thrombosed; and we have already described similar cases, their signs, and symptoms, and I will now describe those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when fully inflamed in the carbuncle, do not appear by touch; only those cured with iron can be seen.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the boil, which one can feel, are those one can treat.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold room, then put the altarul in the tongs, and the root in its roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as ice, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding begins, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranate peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and congeal it with honey and garlic, and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if you cause suction cups to be applied to the back and breasts without injury; then take wool, and mix it with the juice of plantain or of agrimony with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has come to a head, cure the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a bitter almond, so you should cut it as I have said for the thul; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the armpit
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the armpit, such as chancre, stone abscess, herpes, cysts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases as I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It must therefore be said in this treatise on the hot abscess that comes from the liver, which is not among those abscesses that hurt when touched; and if you wish to know the process of making iron, then observe whether the abscess appears at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to puncture it but let it die until the pain is alleviated; and then place the patient on a seat, and have two small seats or cushions for him to recline, supporting his back and aligning his feet with the parts below the leg; and spread his thighs, and place his arms beneath his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then apply the ball towards the right side, and bring it to the instrument through which one works on the mouth of the liver, from which the form will come later; and it must be that when you see the instrument being applied, you insert the point first in order to know the depth of the liver, so that what enters into the instrument does not go more profound than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it must cover the depth of the liver with cloths, so that the instrument does not press upon it; and it must place the trumpet of the instrument above, and touch the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is made soft by hand, you must treat it at the head, with leit spatumile; and when the bowe is emptied, you must put in the wound softened cloths in rose oil, or in green sec oil; and place the cloth out of the wound at the base of the sore, and put above the sore and above the knife a clean wet cloth in water or honey be cooked; then cure after two days of ointment fitting to this, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the sore and the wound by cistere of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and arisologe long be cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed at the sore, you must guard against using iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mestier is first at the birth when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down and desiring to bear: then hasten the child to come forth; know that this childbirth is according to its natural figure, and comes with its head, and the second follows it; and when you see these signs, press lightly on her abdomen so that the child comes quickly; for when it senses above its head, the second follows it, and is cleansed of its impurities by good cleansing; and who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes none other times above its feet, and comes forth in the body or the hips, and the hands, or it comes above the abdomen or sides, and is turned by chance over the neck, and by other evil figures; it is needful for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes down upon his head through natural birth, and the woman delivers easily, and the strength of her body is weak, then place her on a saddle, or let the women hold her; and from its nature, with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, then pour the balm between her two thighs using a small spoon whose form it has.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and scrape away the moist substance that is within; and press her abdomen until the child descends. If it does not descend, then cleanse the woman with a mixture of fenugreek and safflower oil; then have her drink and sneeze condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are fractured, you must reset them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat, and lift her feet high; then take the seat away from the ground, and support the woman so she does not cry out during the resetting; and if the hands cannot be set and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife mentioned earlier, extract the child, and set them evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the extraction of the child from her feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes from her feet, it is necessary to lift it up; then turn it little by little until it is even; then straighten the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps as far as the knees, then one must take hold of it, and cause it to sneeze by pressing; if it is worse, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not worse as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come worse as we have said, take musk of almond, oil of sesamum, and melted gum, and grind them all in a mortar; and put the nature of the woman inside and underneath this ointment, then make her sit in warm water until under her ribs; and when she is softened under, give her myrrh to drink, and put it under, and let her have it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then cause her to sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently rub her abdomen, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child above his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, place your hands on him little by little; then bind his neck, and hang his feet down, and lie on the bed; bend his arms little by little, and then put his hands on his stomach, and remove the cushions under him until she is positioned down; and if the child does not jump, take his feet and move them into shape, then move his stomach upward, then place your hands; and draw the child little by little; and command the woman to hold herself tightly so that the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make lift the woman and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed, and prop up her legs; then administer the ligature as I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and withdraw the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to grip until the infant is issued.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child from its neck, and let her spread her hands, and her face turned towards her mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must have the woman grip her hand, then turn it little by little, and gently; and when it is equal, put on the natural ligature of flax and oil, as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to all the secondine in this manner, cut the secondine with your nail until the moieties are evacuated; and if the pains can be on its face and on its neck, cut from the mouth, do not hold back, and end the pains; then put the child inside, as soon as you have placed it properly, and instruct the woman to bear none again: then gently extract.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins often are born, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not strange nor happens seldom.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are extracted things, and do not live, if few named; I know those, that they be multiplied, and are deprived by the syphilis which devises them, which is linked to the blood; and sometimes sent also naturally as from under the earth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are sent well, the cure as we have said, and be the baths subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does; and make thus as it avails to the health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it should be that the bath know all this, for similar things may happen; do so according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman who has lost a dead child or is in labor, as I have said in the division, and no discharge comes forth, and you are constrained to perform manual work; it must be that you know whether the woman is of sound health and does not have any symptoms or fear of death. It must be that the woman is well supported on her back, with her head inclined downward, and her legs elevated; and the minister places the body on two parts, tying her to the bed so she cannot be moved downwards for the child's descent. Then, rub the inside of the vagina with moist oil mixed with muscilagium of althea and fenugreek, and flaxseed. Next, anoint her hands with these oils and muscilagiums; then gently insert them into the vagina, ensuring that the amount is suitable for this purpose. Be sure to observe whether the child is positioned to descend on its head; if it is, place the oncine in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the forceps or near the sides, and if the descent is through the feet, insert it at mid-back. The minister should insert the oncine into his right hand and place the cord between his left thumb and forefinger, then gently insert them into any of the locations we have mentioned until the thing is empty; this is the form of the oncine.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce against the other pin, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal; and then stretch equally by moving back and forth, to facilitate coming out, and let the pins have teeth to hold them, as is formed here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, open with any of his eye teeth, and push them into that part, and cut the other part; and if there remains none, set this pin or higher up, and do this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by squeezing, then you must wrap it with a cloth, until it all comes out; then cut the cloth at the sole joint or on the side, and thus you must do in the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the outlet is narrow, or it has an acute swelling gathered together, you must place the spatumile spine between your fingers, make a hole in the swelling, and extract the acute; or you can roll it with the instrument called "almidach", which comes from the forms with tools or chapter after this one; and thus similarly do if the child has a large natural swelling; and then pull the bones with the tongs, and if the head suddenly frees itself and is restrained by force, split it until the moist substances that are worse issue out; and if they cannot issue, cut them into pieces as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the back, you must pierce it so that the moist substances flow.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the injury is on his feet, the traction is light, and the direction to the mouth of the artery is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or the breast, it is fitting that you extract it with a silken thread wrapped around the hand; and cut the belly or the breast, as much as the moist parts are contained; and if the other limb is removed, and the head remains, she should hold her hand from the mouth of the artery until it reaches the mouth of the artery; then she should put in one or two drops, and draw forcefully; and if the mouth of the artery is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, it is not fitting to work on it, but it is fitting to administer moist and greasy things; and she should apply poultices, and sitz baths in warm, softening, and moistening substances.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the injury is on his side, and you can place it equal, administer what we have said about the living child; and if one has power, split the wound, and do not leave anything of the secondary.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, administer what we have said for abscesses that come in the thigh, and if bleeding occurs, it should be placed in cold water restraining, and administer other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then sutured the other [one] above it, and caused the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time, an abscess formed in the buttock, and swelled so much that it opened, and caused great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought long, and could not hold the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong吸引力，并从中取出了一些骨头，几天后又取出了其他一些。
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, for the abdomen has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these were the bones of a dead infant.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound, and found bones there, so that the woman was much improved; and the woman lay there for a long time like this, and there was still a bit of blood from it; and I did not remember this chapter only because when the master finds an unusual thing, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After comes the form of the presser, to which the books refer; and to the two turns of the two shoulders.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Firstly, the horns should be finer than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth be two fingers wide, and the margin one finger in thickness, and long a palm and a half; between the two links there should be two adjustments of the same wood, firmly attached on both sides, each half a palm long or a little more; these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open it when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, finer and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of tweezers; it should have two adjustments at the shoulders, as you see, each a palm long and two fingers wide. When you wish to open the marrow with this entire instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread apart. Then insert the two adjustments together into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs. Then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the tweezers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the marrow until the woman does what she desires.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely surmounted, and its likenesses are multiplied; and when the user has prepared them, the work becomes more rapid, and higher in quantity for the people.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not use the instrument without having prepared it, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to seize her abdomen, and then make her snort forcefully, and hold her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she passes it through these means, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a pot and make a hole or cover it. Put herbs that can open the mouth of the mare inside, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, be they cooked or steeped in water on fire. Then place a stick or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare, and hold it until the vapors enter the mare. Then make her snort as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves hastily.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not cured, command the maid to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in almond fat, and then place it in nature, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the bones do not crack during extraction; but it must be moved lightly from right to left, and then cut; it will come and dry out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the joint of the bone is slightly contracted, we have said the treatment for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, then guard that you do not proceed to cut; but it must be that what is at the joint of the bone, you ligate it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with a tetrafarmakon ointment enema; she will take it and put it back in place, and it will become cured; but still, when she takes it, if there comes an不良气味 to the stomach and head, and sickens the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore suitable fumigations are to be used for this: some of the ancients have tested the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is made of glass resembling a cane, and one places the thin end in the nature, and the broad heads above the fire; and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the scab until it is corrupted, and begins another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have their fundament pierced, but have it stuffed with a subtle syfac: then the bailiff must pierce that syfac in its proper place, and not pierce the child with a sharp spatule, and be careful the lancet does not touch; then put on moistened wool in wine and oil, and cure with ointment until healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close up again, place or keep a bandage of lint, and let it remain for a while, and be removed when the child seems ready to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be dealt with suddenly: it should be treated as we have said for the lint bandage.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodules, and grow larger than those coming from the fundament discharge, or in the space between two parts, either one or multiple; and when this nodule is old, it works, and exudes moisture, white pus, or fine granular matter. Sometimes these fistulas are Persian; they are known by those who have them through evacuation or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and by chance during a bowel movement.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if abscesses penetrate to the bladder, and to half the length of the penis; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows whether the abscess is penetrating to the fundament and not: it is that you place your index finger or fundament, and insert a subtle needle of iron or brass into the abscess when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a fine probe or horsehair, as far as you can feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge from the fistula nor windiness nor vermin, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; haste to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is infected up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, then the urine jumps out, and cannot be healed by medications.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it is pierced up to the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes from just above the place; if there are no twists and the source of pain is inside, then it is only a superficial condition, and neither medicine nor immediate ointment curing is effective; in these infected fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the vanity of foolish people who attempt to treat them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	And in those that are neither infected nor ancient, with hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and where the patient lies on their back; lift the legs up to the thighs, and incline the thighs towards the abdomen; then place a tent of wampum or plonc if there are twists, as long as you know where the tent comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep in the fundament, you must place your index finger there; if you then sense that the tendons have been pierced, know that it is penetrated; and if you can discover this between your fingers, whether it be the sphincter or the flesh, know that it is serious; do not attempt to treat it unless you can heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can properly treat some cases, but this happens rarely. The aid we apply, one must heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula as previously said; then insert it hot into the fistula until it comes from the fundament; do this two or three times, until you know that these moistened chars are burned, which resemble a bird's feather; then dress with ointment moistened in grease until the char is gone, and then dress with healing ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus healed and cannot be otherwise healed; and if the tent begins to form but does not penetrate to the depth which is the foundation, and has entered between your finger and the tent a thick covering of flesh or fat, and you see the fistula at that which covers from the beginning of the fistula; cut away from the beginning of the fistula, and apply it before the tent, and cauterize after, until it comes to the head of the tent; then the tent will be delivered, and fall; then debride those fleshy parts that seem like a bird's feather, leaving none remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the healing fails, and cuts between you and the work, cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire, it comprises two good things: that is to say, the burning of these charred pieces, and the stopping of blood and drying out of moisture; then the treatment of wet bandages in butter or ground grease, until the eyes expel the burned matter in mucus; then cure the wound with ointments thick and hardening tough flesh, and are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the point of the foundation and is distant from the body, set a bone or foundation, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tissue, and between them is cloth or skin or charred matter, or it is ready to pierce, there should be no outlets other than a way of hope and faith, by administering one of the three methods: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cut deep down, or if you can, place bandages and treat as first; do not go too far to the point, lest you cut through the tissue that holds the foundation, and let the discharges come out willingly; then treat as we have said; by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it is cut away from the foundation, or with a tent or another pointed instrument; then cleanse the needed char which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and stop the fistula above the foundation: this will be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are treated in this manner: and it is when you puncture the fistula, and it is located next to the foundation beneath the skin, so take a needle pierced through the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you wind the thread twice around it, and insert the needle with the thread into the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is a Persian fistula in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that punctured area, as you would insert your finger or probe; and pull the head of the thread out, and join the two heads together, and hold them tightly against each other, and let them be for one or two days; and hold them once more until the threads close the gaps between them and heal; then treat the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, make it puncture in all the ways that you can, provided it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to cauterize for the ligature if too deep, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spinal fistula is very painful on one side and sharp; and not on the other, for that which should not be cauterized, you do not cauterize, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: some are within the fundament, like grains of resin, and they can be small or large, with blood oozing from them, and there may be one or many, protruding from the fundament and around its edge; but those that are external have little moisture, and only a bit of yellow water or a bit of blood, and their color matches the body. The treatment for those within the fundament is to instruct the patient to rest to expel them, so they can be seen in chambers; when the fundament eases up, and the threads appear, you should act quickly, using tongs or your finger to remove them, then cauterize at their roots. If the uncinus cannot hold them due to their moisture, use a pledget of wool, a cotton swab, or a piece of chamomile cloth; extract them with your fingers, then cauterize and apply warm powders instead of a cautery; or cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization, and treat them with other remedies until they are healed. If the fundament cannot expel them, administer purgative enemas to wash out what is within the fundament, allowing it to come out clearly. When the patient presents, and the threads have fully exited from the fundament, the treatment should be gentle; you should extract them with your fingers or tongs, then cauterize and treat as we have said until they are healed, and prevent incision by metal instruments.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it through a needle, and then pull the thread over and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do so for all the others, leaving one to drain the excess blood; then place a moist cloth in oil of roses or cerote on the foundation, and place it, and command the patient to rest; and let him remain until he convalesces, and when they are healed, apply ointment and other care until he is cured.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dry the wound or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, there is a dry fever in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must reset it at the point of a spike or under your nail, which you should not leave moist; then cure it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot become dry, you must recommence the rasping more forcefully than before, until it heals, and let it become scorched; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small false appearance on the body, and goes very quickly through it. Sometimes when one finds coldness and feels like dying from trembling, it comes throughout the body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a stick from a goose feather, or a very hard vultul feather, and place that stick on the spasm, so that the purple circles cover the entire spasm; then turn your hand with all the stick so that you treat the entire spasm completely, and drive out the spasm to its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do it with a stick of spider web or iron according to this form, and make it thin underneath and drawing over:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, for hold with both hands and press. And if you see, burn the spasm, as is described in the preceding chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the shoulder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Any time the shoulder is dislocated, it is done with silver or iron, or molten brass or bronze; and at any time these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are applied.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the shoulder, whether small or large, is such that the joints are fastened in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it should have a separation or the joints should be fastened as you see, and the head of the shoulder should be pierced through; and it should have two holes on one side and one hole on the other; and place the medicines inside with a bladder of an animal or parchment, and pierce all around with small holes. Place one digit of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread of raw silk in X or about ten places around, and join the joints as if they were a sheep's head; when the medicine is inside, tie it tightly with a strong thread in front of the instrument, then reset it; and this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then prick it lightly; then withdraw the ministers' hands together when it is all dry, then extract the blister, and lift the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine seems to come out, so much as it can; and if he sleeps all night, it will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you blisterize in sickness of stomach discharge, and the medicine hastens to come out, then renew it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is or foundation, or abscess, then let the blister be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle blister where the skin is strained.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds in the division of wound care; now we will speak of hand treatments and medicines according to the procedure.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the parts or places where they are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are through the impact of a stone, or a sword cut, or an axe cut, or a spear, or a javelin, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, because their chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a head injury, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is due to a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound large, and you slightly doubt an abscess hot: so make it soon sanguineous from the cephalic immediately if little blood comes from the wound, and let the sanguineous be on the contrary at the broken part; and avoid the patient's repletion with wine and large foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not turn sanguineous, let the flesh be diminished, and do not drink wine nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if a hot abscess comes, only moist cotton in rose oil or tinctured wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not dried by air or powder, the powder I will say a little later; and if the fire has dried it, place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by stretching, stitch them together, as I will say for wounds of the belly, regarding stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, painful, and holds together only with difficulty, suture it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore firm flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as heads and cooked wheat, like meatballs, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, suture it completely, apply powder, then treat the wound. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, cut without cutting deep, and since it cannot be stopped with medicines, tie the artery with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: it is that you put in this powder which heals as though the mercury had moistened it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live wax three parts, and grind them finely, and apply the powder to the wound, binding it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then clean it well, and leave it unbound unless it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
