Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with just wax, when one does not have incense nor dragon's blood, but lets the mercury moisten the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has cauterized the wound while it was still fresh, one should not put this powder there; but apply some digested ointments, or pulses of flour of barley made with water and honey until they exude whey; then continue to treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other remedy but to leave the treatment, and not put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicines boiled, such as wax washed in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber washed likewise in sweet water, and other mine stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, stitch and bind it with bandages, then treat until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected with worms, pierce or open them lower down. And if an artery is cut, and a bleeding continues, sew it up and cauterize where necessary; and if the spinal cord of the throat is cut, or the vessels, and the channel through which the flesh flows is guarded, then stitch the vessel over the throat bone, and do not touch the throat but set it according to its natural shape. Then bind it properly, let it rest for some days, and treat with dry ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, set it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and leave the rest until the wound rots, and be removed when healed. And if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a sinus, the treatment should be as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or刀伤
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or sword, and the wound is deep, examine if from the wound there is any sign that the patient will die: then you know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, but fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder at the first hour, nor let it dry completely for the blood to not demerge into the heart and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bandage it 2 times a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to drain the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; so there will be no convulsion, nor male tremor of the heart or any other signs of death; and when you see good disposition, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure therefore the sores and other treatments until he is healed; and if it cannot heal, operate, then you know there is a fistula; treat the wound as we should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple or worse on the back, treat the part in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, treat with powder; and if it is close to the bone and has cut pieces, clean the wound, remove any loose threads; and if they are not loose, let the wound drain, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	for the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the abdomen are great and medium and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because we cannot place the intestines back in without heating them; for when they feel cold, they shrink back in, and for this reason, the medium-sized wound is better, as we reheat the intestines to their proper place. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the abdomen, and the suture of other wounds on the body and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; however, they are more appropriate with the suture of the abdomen, and I will say each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no internal thing is injured, and it is easy to remedy, this can be done by one of two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in a proper manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth in warm water only, or you can cook it in warm water with quince and cypress and spice, and apply it to the intestine until the swelling is removed; and once this astringent wine has been applied, let it dry for deswelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or cooked hellebore and malva, for by these it is alleviated at the entrance of a small thing; and if nothing can enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to remove hemorrhoids; and let the first cure be dry before cutting, as we should not cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument to cut: so slice internally along the curve and do not go too deep, and see here the form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have protruded, replace them backward according to their natural form in their proper place if you can, for this is correct.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the area below the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the area above the abdomen, raise the head and buttocks higher than the other parts. And similarly, if the abdominal rupture is in one of the two areas, place them so that the severed part is higher than the other; and thus you should treat as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is provided to you. Have the minister of pitoys (a type of herbal medicine) at hand who can cover the entire wound with their hand and close its edges; this is a common method of suturing, where you take an needle or several needles according to the width of the wound. Leave a finger's breadth from the edge of the wound, insert one needle with strong thread into it; pierce both sides of the skin with two needles, which are inside the skin, until the part is fully pierced, then assemble the three ends of the siphac (a type of ligature). Next, pass a double thread through the needle from both sides, and assemble the edges of the wound accordingly. Then leave a finger's breadth again, insert another needle; join the thread as you did with the first needle, without ceasing to do so according to your need for needles until the entire wound is sutured. Use medium-sized needles, neither too fine nor too large, because very fine needles may cut all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot easily enter: therefore, they should be medium-sized. Do not insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin so as to avoid cutting the wound before suturing. Afterward, remove the ends of the needles to prevent them from irritating the patient during sleep, and cover the needle ends with a small cloth or bandage for better holding, leaving them until the wound is healed; this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for smaller wounds as one needle suffices for a second suture. And you should assemble the two skin sides and the two siphac (ligature) on one needle with strong medium thread; when you have pierced these ends all four together, reduce the needle to the part where you began, in the manner of threading cloth; keep a distance between each suture equal to a finger's breadth. This type of suture can be seen by others, and I once sewed a wound on someone who had been cut with a knife, where the wound was more than a palm wide, and contained intestines twice as large, located in the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I restored his intestines after twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the midwife had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and placed old cloth on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing: take the needle, and thread it from the outer part to the inner; when it has pierced through the core straight on, leave the head of the siphon or stitch or where you threaded the needle, and make it pierce again from the inner part to the outer. The understanding of this stitching is that you sew as a tailor would sew fur, leaving the siphon on one side once, and coming back to it from another direction until the sewing is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen stated precisely, is such that no one does not perform it, who brings together the two parts naturally and applies one chief of silk thread to the other chief, in this manner: place an awl or chief of needle near, and make a single piercing through that side, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the awl, and make it pierce from the part from below until within, at the two ends of the silk; and this is the better method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and no one testifies against it, that one should sew the abdomen with two needles, each having thread; and one should cast one needle from one part, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corruptions; and know that when the wound is within the abdomen, the suturing is more grievous than on other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as the surgeon has made it bleed, so you return the intestines, and the gut. Then put on the powder promoting flesh, and if the surgeon has made it bleed, then put on any ointment that is present until the wound heals; bind the threads, let the sutures, and the catgut be sewn up; then cure the wound as with others until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on old cotton immediately when it begins to run pus, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, then it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered heat oil or in rose oil, and put it between the layers, and under the flaps; and if it feels pain or corruption in blisters, and often happens, so cleanse with black wine enemas, and especially if the corruption comes to the intestines; and puncture internally, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is due to the veins that are in it, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the spleen jumps from the wound, reset it behind in the same way as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned brown or black, then you must tie the part that is black, to prevent blood from flowing, because there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ties, and place both shoulders below the part beneath the wound until over to facilitate the extraction when the spleens fall, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, one can restore it in some people, for I saw a man who was wounded by a lance in his right side of the stomach; the wound became ulcerated and turned into a fistula, from which emissions and wind issues; I treated it as best as I could, and continued to cauterize until it healed, and the wounds were stitched.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his stomach; and there was no pain at all, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking well; and some experimentors said that for a small wound in the intestines, it must be bound in such a manner: take a piece of cloth with large holes, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the cloth has opened the mouth, put it on the two edges, so that it clings to the mouth; then close the top, and this holds so that it cannot be undone, then put another piece of cloth in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered; then suture the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is burned in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, one can ligate the intestine with a fine thread made from the intestine of an animal in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is most undamaged, then tie it at the head of this thread with a thin linen thread twisted, then put the thread on the needle and suture the intestine, and secure it at the rupture; and this way of suturing for straining is only according to hope and faith; and there is no remedy if the wound is large and wide, especially in one of the large intestines.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals over time, is universally called a "fistula," and especially when it is closed and grows back.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation hard and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also hairy like a bird's feather; sometimes clear hollow, and at other times thick; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only forth by one of the nine causes: namely, due to the smallness of the blood or corruption; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and over the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the bones are rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the nature of the region, digestion is delayed, health is late, and swelled by nature; or there are veins or bone: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it must be that I tell you about the treatment of fistula which is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula can occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the throat, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and so it is such that it affects the primary property of the body part.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas of this kind are of serious concern for health, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the surface until it reaches what I have said, and you trust in its cure, and you can recognize it, take a tent of copper or iron, if the fistula is straight, hold it against it; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it with a fine tent of linen, for the linen will fold around the curvature. And if the fistula has openings and you cannot thoroughly examine it with tents, cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, for moisture conducts easily from one opening to another and cleanses them; then firmly press it with your hand that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and whether it is well healed, and ask the patient where he feels pain when pressed, and locate the exact place; and when you truly know its location, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the places I have mentioned, treat it as I have said, and remove the false tissue and decayed flesh that are within; and then continue to treat it until it is healed. And if the fistula is deeply seated in the right place, you must thoroughly cauterize it as much as you can, and then insert moist cloths medicated with water, placing them up to the head of the fistula until the medicine erodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and afterward apply healing ointments containing healthy flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is decayed due to the fistula, treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve is not injured or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king (the wound) be cleaned until all the corruption is removed, then cure the flesh around the wound until it is healed; and if it is not healed, return to binding as before: know that you have not yet reached the root of the matter. So uncover and clean thoroughly until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then set the bone right; and if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If the corruption is too deep, you cannot remedy it; then there is no other means but to leave it to nature. And if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with forceps, do so with an appropriate instrument. And if there are many bones, extract them all, leaving none behind. And if moisture opposes this, and there is neither error nor fear, cut away the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if thou canst not remove them within an hour, put upon the wound something that corrupts pus, and let it remain until the flesh is corrupted throughout the bone, and then the bones will be easier to reset; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, reset only the corruption until the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is much corrupt part, reaching the marrow of the bone; thou must scrape and cut all down to the corruption, and then cure until it be joined. And I will tell thee of a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that thou mayest take example and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years of age, who had pain in his leg from a cause within the body, such that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess. There was no clear reason to open it; but the monks, out of their folly, opened it so much that the abscesses were opened, and much matter flowed out, and became a fistula. Many wounds appeared from which great amounts of pus and moisture came from the body; and many monks applied treatments for over two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands until I was called. I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what flowed from the holes caused a great stench; and the skin of the young man turned red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one went against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the holes enough to discover a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with corruption extending to the inner bone; I saw what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, but what I removed; and began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; then I began again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and sawed it out, and pondered how to mend the place; but I could not do so until I cut into about a palm's breadth of the bone, which was completely removed, then restored with medicines; and it was healed and quickly sewn, and there was no need to restart the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and out of fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the bleeding often occurs during evacuation, but it was completely healed, and in the place of the bone a hard scar formed, and it was well disposed and had no harm or adverse effect at all, neither externally nor internally.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a ligature, and draw it tightly around the end of the bone that protrudes, and command someone to extend it upwards; place another larger ligature of linen over the scar above the bone, and tighten the ends, so that you pull the corrupt flesh away from the bone, and uncover the flesh at the site where you wish to operate without letting the bone blacken the flesh; put a stick or board under the bone to help remove the corruption; it should be done as much as can be seen and felt of the corruption, and also again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or part thereof, uncover the flesh completely; then place a hot coal under it, and afterwards stretch the corruption from one part to another with strips of skin as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut out the corrupted joint, and replace the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no old custom but to use copper; and if the corruption is near the knife of the hand or the knife of the foot, it is very strong, but still you must inquire about that corruption as to how it appears; and cleanse it in all ways possible, but so that the vein or nerve does not oppose you; and know that the incisor and skin strips for coppering these bones are many, according to the alignment of the bones and their appearance, and their size and subtlety, and their strength and weakness; and for this reason, it is necessary to prepare an instrument appropriate to each form of work; and know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the methods of diseases; so consider the tool you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder dislocates either internally or externally; and when you have medicated the corruption by cleaning with medicines, and it does not improve, then you must treat that limb until the site where the corruption arises, so that the patient escapes from death, or from the greater malice of the limb's defect; and the signs are that the limb turns black, seeming as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness comes, the corruption spreads from limb to limb throughout the body; so hasten the treatment, and if it is due to the sting of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar, and the corruption is at the head of the arm, then treat it, and do not give it space to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes as far as the hand, fix at the joint, so that the corruption does not come as far as the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except according to its quantity of virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes to the first joint, fix after the other joint; and if it pierces, fix the whole piercing; and if it rises in the leg, fix at the joint below the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of fixing or healing the limb is that you tie it above and below, extend some ministers one line down, and others ministers one line up, and you cut the flesh which is between the two lines at a spathe width, so that the bone be uncovered; then fix or heal, and put a linen bandage on each side, so that the sinew does not touch the healthy bone, and cause another lesion and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the bleeding comes when you work, cauterize the limb hastily, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, and bind the injured member with an adequate bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man: he had a dark spot that seemed like fire burn, and this corrosion came first on his big toe of the foot, so much so that it encompassed all the foot; and when the doctor saw the corruption, he hastened to treat the foot, and was healed; soon after, the same corrosion returned on his toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I placed reflectors after purifying the body, but the corrosion did not cease; he asked that I amputate his hand, and I refused, for I had hope of reflecting the matter; I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, since the strength of a man was weak; he became desperate and returned to his land, hastening to treat his hand, and was healed; and I did not recount this story except for when one needs another such thing.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess arises in the flesh, and stays so long that it gathers great masses of pus; then it rots and perforates, and the pus leaps out, leaving the bones visible, as if they were vessels; the skin above is as delicate as torn silk, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain" and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in full length, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you peel away all of this skin, especially when it is delicate, as if it were torn silk; and it does not rupture because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you find that the skin is peeling and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with a medicated enema in this way: first, observe whether the swelling is large and the pus has a foul smell; then prepare an Egyptian medicine as follows: take aloe, oil of roses, and litharge, equal parts, and boil them together in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then use it according to your need, mixing it with water and honey, and apply it to the swelling, pressing on the abscess; let the medicine remain for two hours, then express and remove it. Do this repeatedly until the swelling is reduced and the pus is removed. If such medicine is not available, you can use an enema of ash water; take ashes from vine branches, pour water over them, strain the liquid, and apply it as an enema. Continue until you see that the swelling has been thoroughly cleansed. If the patient cannot tolerate this or if neither the Egyptian nor the ash water medicine works, prepare a honey and vinegar enema with some litharge; or use honey and wine, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine helps the abscess rupture. After doing this, if you find that the swelling is thoroughly cleansed, apply a plaster that promotes flesh growth in it, using rose oil and wine for preparation. Or apply other medicines and ointments whose properties I have mentioned when discussing ointments; if the opening of the breast is small and the enema cannot enter, enlarge it slightly with a sharp object, and insert a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it fits properly. If the wound is too large, close it off so that only enough space remains for the enema to pass through. And if the opening from which pus comes is on top, apply the ointment or more below where it is located.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is fully drawn, do not allow it to release any flesh; and if you cannot cut through the skin as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bow runs as low as possible where it is. For when the bow is fully drawn, do not allow it to release any flesh and if you cannot cut through the skin as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner: that the bow runs lightly downward, and leave nothing of the bow; and take consolidative medicines to put over the sound part, and keep them under a linen cloth that covers all the sound part; then cut with force toward the hole in the chest slightly wider than the first, for ointment should be applied underneath the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the hole in the healthy part to ease the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once; and that which is beneath the hole in the chest, often remove to release the bow, and know what flows from the bow, whether it is venom or little or enough, or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that stands over the hole in the healthy part, know that the breasts are now expanding, and approach health; and then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels undigested bow (a term likely referring to a kind of food or substance) after many days, know that the breast does not decay.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For it is in men who have delayed healing of their wounds for a long time, and in those who do the opposite; and if undigested food suddenly comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not decay; and if the breast delays healing and is far away, apply drying medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as anointing diaphoretic, for there is a large part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and pour it with equal wine in substance; then let it infuse and use it; and the same thing works better when cooked grease is used instead, when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and frankincense, and grind them on honey while they are on fire; and then wrap them in a cloth, and place them on the breast, and sometimes administer long-liver roots, which are as fine as flour of wheat and centory; and use simples or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, and put it on the honey as I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption is complete and affects the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; so treat the fistula of the cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Pannaritis is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or foot, or sometimes it may arise in other toes; and when it becomes matured and is not attended to, it comes to a head, boils, and pours out pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes even all of it; and causes corrosion extending to the bone, causing painful inflammation of the finger, with the color turning foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the remaining nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are much great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses upon the flesh and begins to prick it, and the blisters, then you must put a cloth under the nail that does not touch the flesh, and let the blisters rise up, and cut away that subtle and light flesh, and apply medicines burning and corrosive for removing all of it; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out forcefully, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone decayed, cut it away as previously mentioned, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is infected and swells up, and it feels great pain, you must first cleanse it; then trim the nail with a sharp spatule cutting across, making sure the cuts do not come to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something above that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain comes from the ear of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Li must adjust those that arise in the hands of some men by accident and are either all fleshy, or have a division or bones, and sometimes an nail, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of our bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which arises in any bone of the hand does not move, and that which arises at the joint of the hand, by accident, may move; the size of that which is fleshy is light, in a manner such: cut it at its root with a broad scalpel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is grievous to treat: if you hold it with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or must be done last, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate tool, and cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that arise from these injuries come either by birth, or suddenly from a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut that sore, so that it heals according to its natural form; then place between two moist cloths or soft drapes in olive oil, preventing them from adhering; or you place between two fine pieces of linen, until the edges are sewn as they should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the symptoms come with either of these two using the palm [of the hand], cut that sore as necessary.
des vils	of the wretched
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	When his veins are swollen enveloped with excessive melancholic humours, coming from many members of the body; and more occurs in legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer one time purgation of colic, and then heal him with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is according to two methods: one is where they cauterize and cut or let the black blood flow; and the other method is that you open the vein and let it bleed completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: first, heat the leg with hot water greatly, until the flesh becomes tender. Then, stretch the patient's leg from below the knee to the part just above the kneecap; next, incise the vein at one place, or two, or three, making a wide cut. Then lift and let the black blood flow by hand from one end to the other, until as much blood has flowed as the virtues of the patient can bear; then bind it, and instruct the patient to dye his skin with meat juices that seep black colic. And repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment is conducted in this manner: realign the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then immerse it in a bath. Then raise the leg with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire, and place a cloth along the length of the vein from the lower part of the knee to just above the ankle; then open the skin inch by inch, and burn the vein on each side until it appears when touched; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters or exits the skin it seems like a white cord; then place a cloth underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then let it down gently, then place another cloth above three fingers; then burn the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the cloth as you did before, and let it down on another inch, just like you did first; then cut a different size, or more if needed, then lift it, and cut at the toe part, then draw and lift until reaching the second size; then remove by size in size until it is all out, then cut; and if you cannot pull and lift it, place a needle with a strong double thread underneath, and tie and draw, and place underneath the cloth, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; and keep it from cutting, for if it cuts, you cannot pull or lift it, and this harms the patient; and when you have treated all of it, then put moistened wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the area of the wound, and treat until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is twisted and tangled together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cut through it completely; and pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut completely, so as not to cut the vein; and it is of large curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it is large as we have said, and this is its form.
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is interwoven in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from putrefaction that comes beneath the skin, as serpents and worms come within the body, intertwining between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg, then change the eyes, and begin the vein to issue forth, as one root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder is opened, it covines that you envelop around a piece of lint one and a half to two inches long, and the wick, and leave the lint hanging on the leg, and every time there is none at the end, you envelop around the lint and the wick; and if it is too long, you cut a part of it, and envelop the remainder, and do not cut it near its root, so that it remains entirely issued; for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess, putrefaction, or tumor; because of this matter, it covines that it be treated little by little until full, and nothing remain or core; and sometimes this vein, when it is treated from five inches long, or ten, and a rod's length, came to me, from which it issued ten inches long, and when you cut it, you insert one raisin or pertus, and pierce it thoroughly so that all issues out; and let the matter inside be drained, and administer on the tumor medicines preventing putrefaction any day, then cure it as the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes there are small wounds, and especially when they appear in the joint of the foot or hand, and it comes much from punctures; cure them therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle boil," because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm which arises between skin and flesh, and goes upward and downward throughout the body, and one feels it well as it travels from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and exits forcefully; and it is nourished by putrefaction of some humors, such as come from serpents and worms and ascarids or intestines; and doubt arises about its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot force it when it goes: therefore, you must tie the limb above and below with a strong thread tightly, then cover over and drain it out, and if the pus is fully present in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm it does is that it will run into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, restrain strongly beneath it, then cover over, and drain it out; and the patient must use cleansing of the body with medicinal solutions for foul humors, and beware of meats causing putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those whom I tell this.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like live silver when it is cut from another; the pain left that one and sank into the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it returned repeatedly within her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how it moved in this manner from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
