Firstly, I had wished that they truly wanted to move their pain away from the head to another part of the body, but I did not wish it as much as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a solid body, with veins uncovered, and because these winds were constrained and appeared not according to this reason to those who have soft bodies and moist veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see the treatment of this disease, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, scrape away the pus above and below hastily, and then clean until those constrained winds at the site are gone; and cauterize the area. And if you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it with substances that expel winds, such as bitter pills and blistering herbs, and others like them.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various types, according to their shapes and the parts of the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their shape is that some have large points, and small ones, and feathery ones, and those fused together; and some have two angles, and those with tongues, and some with pieces. Those which lodge in any limb do so in different ways: sometimes in a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it lodges in any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear: then you must be wary of extracting this arrow, for death often follows such dispositions; and when none of these bad signs are apparent, and the arrow is not fully embedded, you should extract it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the head when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and starts a swelling which is above the head, is when there is scotomia and stiffness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes it is without force from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes affects speech and voice; and starts a wound with moist white discharge seeming like a pulse, and also as if boiled flesh; and if this sign appears to you, keep from treatment, and extract the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; sometimes the arrow moves like a pulse, and brings dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never left the body is that without any drops of pus it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes loudly and warms up.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the cover of the foot, it affects the small bones; it causes great pain and breathlessness; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls on the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly, and it jumps out leaving no hay along the intestinal tract, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine sprays out and stops flowing, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the humerus and the thigh and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into the nose at its root: I drew it out, and pulled it from the other side under the ear's fat, and he was cured without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was embedded, and could not be reached except by the point toward the wood, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, light as iron without ears; the wound healed, and no bad accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with ears: I extracted the barbs, and drew it out carefully, and the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew out an arrow from the man, who was either in his chest or abdomen, and thought he would die; and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change. I incised the arrow, treated it, and extracted it, and suffered no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow fall or hit him, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural position, nor caused any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man, who had an arrow fall into his face, and the wound was sewn up; and remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow that fell upon a man of the king's household, which struck among the joints, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely pierced. I was called for the treatment after it fell three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I treated it with a fine thread, and did not feel it; yet there was a puncture and pain beside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a plaster of atratifactive and digestive ingredients on his eye, because the eyes did not swell; and the eye appeared to be affected by the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster for several days, and redressed the wound again. The patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow within his nose on the following day; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open. I tested it and felt the head of the arrow decaying in the eye; then I continued to treat the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and passed through well within four months, and then cleared the wound so that I could use forceps to extract it from both sides, but it would not come out. Then I continued to experiment and devise methods with various instruments until I successfully extracted it using properly made forceps on one day, as described in the form at the end of this chapter, as I treated it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I will restore it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or have I told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you apply your cure to what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but wise masters compare on very little, and on what is present and lacking, find nine operations, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are in the members where they are stuck in two ways: either by the place where they enter, or from another side; and the one that enters through the place where it enters is an arrow piercing the flesh, and is not stuck more than once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the flesh rots away entirely, and then the issue will come out; and also if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, let it stay for some days, changing it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce through to all the innermost parts with a fine needle, until the flesh inside is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the brain's ventricles, or any of the conditions I have said to the patient: do not treat it at all, but let it be until it becomes equal after some days, for if the arrow comes just to the syrinx, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is pierced only into the bone and not to the surface, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the means of extracting it should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply pierced and cannot be withdrawn forcefully, then I administer tar externally, as I have said; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the flesh so that it cannot be seen, then seek it thoroughly throughout the body; and if you feel it, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and extract the arrow if possible, and if there are feathers attached to the arrow that it holds, remove the flesh embedded on both sides up to the part you can reach, and then break or bend the feathers of the arrow so you can extract it; and take great care not to break the arrow, as you would extract it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it be until the flesh between the bones becomes rotten, then remove it, for the extraction is inflammation.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding contrary to your expectation makes you do otherwise, follow what we have said about the treatment in this chapter; and guard against incising the nerve or the vein, and move it as you can to extract the arrow without peril, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, or where it penetrates something, or the skin is swollen so one can see or feel it: incise there, as deep as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it is now stuck.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push the entire shaft; and if the shaft falls, and you see need to administer a thrust, then apply the tool point entering in, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the tool; and then push, and if the arrow is stuck, then push the tool with the point entering in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or pierces in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, and you can reach it, then extract it; and guard against reaching the vein or the nerve, and then extract it, and then suture the wound if necessary; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for extracting arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle used for piercing is also similar to the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for putting out and for knowing so is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins through which one is cured are thirty-one, of which sixteen are principal, namely: two jugulars which are behind the ears and called "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the temples and visible; and the veins that are in the lacrimal glands of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that runs along the forehead; and the vein that is on the nose; and the two subclavian veins which are at the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one draws blood commonly are: in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it lies on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fase," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and it lies over the flexile, and it is this one from which bloodletting is done, which clearly appears above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The savattel vein is the vein that lies between the auricular and annular spaces, and it has two veins; in the leg and foot are three veins: one of them is below the curve of the pouch on the left side, and the second sophene vein which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nese" that is in the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the vein, as I say, is that you reset the patient's head, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then fix the patient's neck to a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two loops dependent on the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, prick it; then take the lancet, put it beneath the vein until the bone, lift your hand up the entire vein, cut and remove the skin and the vein very deeply twice through, and let the blood flow out until you see it; then close it up tightly until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good for migraines from old age, stiffness, and long-term eye strain, and for the body's watery tears in the eyes; and the quality of this treatment is as I say: and it is that the patient clenches his neck so much that the two veins are clearly visible; and feels a pulse under your thumb, then sighs deeply; then lift the heart above the vein to the top with your index finger, insert the lancet underneath, lift the vein upwards, and the cloth, as you did in the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on a cotton pad; and then form it properly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them regarding their tying and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The health of the vein on the forehead is as important as that of the cephalic for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness; and its quality is such that diseases draw their cord by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is described here:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the disease from its hold, and bind the vein until it is sound, and never work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In all ways, it is not fitting that the flames be too hot; and let the vein be transversely positioned, for the bone is nearby, and by chance the flame might break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps with the eyes, and with hives, and with redness, and with the inner part of the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the qualities of their health are such that the patient draws his coltis (a kind of worm or louse) out by twisting at some point, as was said before; then the savior, and let the savior through the traverse be a bit long like a flame a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then cause the blood to flow as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein of the nose is good for water and soda frostbite, and diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that come to the face, especially when it is old; and the qualities of the health are such that the patient draws his coltis (a kind of worm or louse) out by twisting at some point with his left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and sticks it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well initially, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too far to perfection, and cause the blood to flow as much as your need requires, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The health of the two glands aids in narrowing the larynx, and in the beginning of mixture, and much disease, and pettiness, and corrosion, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the health is that the patient expels his throat from under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient's head, and the patient lie on the seat, then make a cut along the vein somewhat widely, then draw off the blood moderately, or as need requires; then do the same elsewhere in another vein, then untie the bandage, and press moderately all the veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the glands
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the lips above help in swelling in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and around the nose and between the lips.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are such that they make the patient sit facing you, and press his lip as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and you recognize them by their blackness, and by the fact that around them are fine black veins: cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and similarly treat the two veins above and below, for they are of the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the health of the cephalic vein, and this is in narrowing the throat, and diseases of the uvea, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sainie is that the patient's pain subsides before your eyes in the sunlight, and it eases the tongue, and you look beneath on each side a black vein: therefore both are healthy, and do not go too much for perfect health, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the tongue that are commonly treated can be healed in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp thorn or with a fine olive stick, which is called "anesil"; and they are large and fine according to the size and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flint flame is much renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has need to open veins filled with large amounts of apparent blood, and contain large amounts of thick blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed subtle, and is for cleansing subtle veins, or where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the collarbone, and in the ribs, and in the abdomen; and it is suitable for the surgeon who needs to bleed and avoid the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the artery, and bleeding comes, then it must be stopped as I have said; and one should not press with fire, but cut as with a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and replace another; or if you want any hair from it, or you wish to insert a vein into the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with the fire knife as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the wound, then you must extract the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a needle, and then tie the arm, and incise the vein with the fire knife; and beware that you do not wound the artery when you see the place swollen, for this is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see bulging upwards as urine from a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is blood vessels: then hasten, and place your finger lengthwise, then remove your finger when the veins have stopped, for this often happens; if the patient's arm is injured, leave it thus, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins are not stopped, and it hurts you, and the medicines are not at hand, cut the artery if it appears, for the head of the arrow is there; stop the veins.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark from the fig tree, split it, and take one half and tie it well just until the other day; if the veins stop, that is good; if not, treat the wound as we have said, using powders to stop bleeding; but the dressings are not grievous for many conditions of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein in the middle helps to draw blood from above the head and below the body, because it is composed of basilique and cephalique, as we have said; and for the patient it is necessary to guard against the nerve beneath, and if too closely punctured, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the health is damaged, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, it is fitting that you anesthetize the part with the instrument before puncturing; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalique vein helps, drawing blood from the head and aiding the eyes; it is necessary to puncture with olive oil flame or myrtle oil flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as it does not have any nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Firstly, you should seek the lightest weight stone, and do not harm anything if it does not work the first time, and then repeat; and by chance, the stones swell in some people, when it does not work the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sinew is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about sinew is that sinew should be drawn only to preserve health and to avoid future diseases; and the sinew should be taken from one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of prayers on bended knees, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and it should be done on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The medicine that is administered for diseases has no fixed hour determined, but when need is of day or nourishment, at all hours and in all times; and it is not fitting to medicate children up to fourteen years, nor women with child from four months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be medicated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when any wish to be medicated, in whatever manner it may be, it is fitting that he purge the intestines with a light enema if there is much fluid retained, so that the veins do not attract from the intestines the superfluous putrid matter harmful to the principal limbs; nor should one medicate those who are too much salted by meat, nor those who are drunk, whether they be strong in drink, nor those who are dropsy cases. And if one wishes to medicate after colic attack, vomiting, and evacuation of the belly, or increase of frequency of intercourse, work, staying awake, fasting, or those who have lost much of their strength by arm or body injury; then with subtlety of the humors, if the vein is large, due to meat, drink, and medicines, if you have the power; then before an enema, if any such thing does not prevent it, for subtletizing the blood, and one medicates from the vein between the toes into the third toe, as we have said; and on that day avoid work, labor, and lust, and similar things. Be bound and joined, and let the medicator be higher than whom you are medicating, and rub your arm two or three times, then extract the thread moderately above the midpoint, for when it is too tight or loose, blood cannot flow; and then rub the vein with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them. Then anoint the medicator's finger with a little old oil, then place his left hand just below the vein over which he wishes to medicate, ensuring the vein does not get injured by the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as strings in the veins, and some that are full of windiness, such that when one applies fire to them, they recoil from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one belongs to those; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the physicians must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; but if not, he should attempt to open it again slightly below or above that place, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen and the patient feels discomfort, let him rest for one or two days without binding his arm: perhaps abscesses will form. Do not enter a bath, but proceed with the operation if he wishes; and if the opening is small, or the skin is thin and you doubt whether there is as much blood as you see, apply the flame directly to that opening; work quickly, while the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the joint swollen, do not begin the healing anew, and place a bit of oil-juice on it, for it lightens the body from blood, and makes the oil's juice move in this joint; thus administer oil-juice in each healing where you heal veins, to stop the course of blood; and the same is done with triacle and bovine gall when placed on the joint; so subtlely do the juices part when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is not healed the first time or when the opening of the vein is small, you should hasten and place a wet sponge in cold water and warm salt on the joint for an hour; and you must do this after the blood from the vein has drained. And if any black or green color remains on the joint after several days, it does no harm; and if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh set in calamus, resin, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance on the flesh of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for chance may cut into an artery; but make it a dry poultice to harden the area, and then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each of the humors according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, that one make a larger wound, and let the flints be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and let it heal little but often, and should heal by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is saved from running of blood and compression of nerve, and is better than long or large wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body requires nourishment during the healing, it is fitting to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, draw off three or four times blood. And if he has a cold constitution, eat before the healing soft bread soaked in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells in the side, after the discharge of much blood, it is fitting that he inhales broth of flesh and fragrant subtle syrup, and uses the other things we have said in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees fit to let the arm swell and swell again, when he is weakened by great swelling, it is fitting that he be made to swell a little and a little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who sees fit to let the arm swell after the first swelling, and if it has strong currents, he should be made to swell seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever is to be healed from another part, must be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and it brings fever; so it must be treated by drawing a great quantity, and widening the puncture until it chiefelems with pus; then when you reward all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on his pulse as he heals, that death not come in lieu of chiefelemling, and this happens many times, when the healers are negligent; and must not when you see release the arm, and make the blood issue the second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is crooked, that you extend the arm hastily, for that would be ill; but let it be until it heals the second time; or thou applyest at the point of the flame, until the one who is congealed to the puncture from the vein issues forth, and put there a little salt moistened in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to treat the blood a second time, let the vein be in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein on the hand because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of treating it is that the patient should hold their hand in hot water until the fingers turn red; then tie it moderately so that the vein is clearly visible, and now siphon the blood from the middle, neither from the wide part nor the long part; and make the punctures large, and siphon the blood close to the joint of the hand, and if there is no blood coming out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not repeatedly dip the hand in hot water, as it should be used more in winter than in summer; and siphoning from this vein is safer than from any other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The health of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: stretch the hand, and pour in hot water, until the veins are swollen, if one sees them; and if the hand is crooked, and if you correct it completely, then you do not grieve anything; and do not go too fully perfect, for the nerve are beneath all naked of flesh, and then put the hand in hot water, if the hand is frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn enough blood as needed, put a piece of oil-soaked cloth on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each finger.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the thing in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse (likely referring to a type of abscess or swelling), and do everything as I have said for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The illnesses of the spleen are useful for all diseases that are beneath the body, such as liver diseases, retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its medicine are that diseases expel stones in hot water, and rub on the vein until it swells, and tie above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot much rain goes; therefore heal or a larger vein, or at the ankle, which moves well.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves beneath, and heal through them as when cutting; let the flambes be asbestos.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the stone cannot come out, place the foot in the water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the stone is needed for the first time, begin again the second time slightly above it, because the leeches are salted; nor doubt of nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the sponge on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leech for the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the stronger side, and its stone is worth for the pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its stone is such that the patient should enter the bath, and squeeze four times above the ankle, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, apply the stone in all ways you can, and by crossing it; and move it much as you can, for the leech is loose, and it is very responsive to manual application.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, trace any vein from the front or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let the bleeding continue as much as you see, and then undo the bandage, and place a cotton pad and bind it; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	Of the suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without piercing is done in two ways: either by fire or without fire; and the suction performed by piercing and drawing blood is done at fourteen places on the body, of which one is placed at the neck; another is inserted into the armpit; two are placed on both sides of the neck; a suction cup below the chin; a suction cup on both shoulders; a suction cup on the hips; suction cups between both arms; suction cups on both legs; suction cups on both ankles; and fire suction does not draw blood, but only minor veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason, it weakens none at all, as one would do with a vein from a vein puncture; nor is it appropriate to administer it by fire or without fire in any disease that comes from overfullness, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is proper to bloodlet, or for custom, we will perform it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between times; for there are such as, when they have need to bloodlet, have a heavy head; and there are such who find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and draw blood; and there are such who think, and see by vision of blood and pain and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially between the hours of the month, we command them to bloodlet after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinew of the muscle aids in the weakening of the head’s chief... that comes to them, and it is not fitting that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is at the site of the sinew of the cephalic, and it is not fitting that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have catarrh, for it does them much harm; because of this it is not fitting that the watchmen use it, nor those who have or chief cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often heals with it becomes forgetful, and because of this, it is necessary to place the suction cup a bit lower due to the forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation at the neck is at the site of the sinew of the head and the basilica, and because of this, it is effective for narrowing of the vein, and cutting of the channel of the subclavian, and soon, and for fullness; and it should be applied only briefly, for if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind movements over the second ribs of the neck cause pain in the head, eye disease, and migraines, and stranglement, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is located in the healthy part of the basilica; and you must instruct the surgeon that he should extend his hand when placing, not cut the artery, and avoid hemorrhages.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind movements around the chin cause mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and are located in the healthy parts of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind movements in the shoulders cause illness that comes from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind movements in the groins are as significant as those of the three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to cut too closely to them, for the tissues are bare of flesh, and one can feel the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping device placed on the buttock treats hemorrhoids from below and internal diseases, and it should be large, made of iron, and well-treated; otherwise, if it were fine, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping on the legs heals openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are effective for old pains in the knees, hips, and bladder, and reduce swelling; and they are placed on the two ankles and the two calves, and in any case, they weaken the body after long use, and bring paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping device is to first ensure it is empty and then gently warm it. Place it quickly and move it evenly without stopping until you see the area turn red and swell, indicating the appearance of blood color. Then remove it, reapply the cups, and be mindful of the body's disposition, for some have thicker skin with clearer pores; in such cases, you should only prick once, making large but shallow wounds. Suck gently if necessary.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it must be pricked twice: the first time to facilitate the passage of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very full, it must be pricked three times; and when we wish to draw a little blood at a time, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw much blood, we begin often; and if the vein is full, prick it thoroughly, and the points should be pierced suddenly, and for those with thick skin and hardness, and who have narrow pores, you should anoint the eyes of the suction cups with a pungent and dissolving oil: if it is in heat, use olive oil or sweet almond oil or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in cold, use mustard oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile oil, or some other similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take bitter aloes, or balsam, or oil of anise, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is to be healed has tight flesh and narrow pores, it is not necessary to put oil there, but it should be washed after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or hawthorn water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from almond, or hawthorn water, or sumach water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or puke water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to heal with suction cups before the bath nor during the bath, but after the bath one hour or two; and do not sleep after ventilation, and he should be wrapped when he is to be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch over those who are healing and are choleric, and if the blood is too hot and inflamed; then it must take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eats grubs, and flesh of capon, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and moderately fragrant wine between evening and morning, and eats little, and eats grubs and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men treacle or mace before or after cupping to support the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the thigh, and in gout, and on the abdomen and mouth and ribs and hip, for these parts do not endure being pierced at their roots, and one does this with fire only to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on nipples when a child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place suction cups on the abdomen and on the mouth to alleviate the member; and removes pain, when there is swelling or stone, it may remove the swelling or extract the stone from its place; thus does it when placed on the liver and on the thigh when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck solely; sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such manner we fill the cup with warm water or with water after cooking suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm deep, and have or cut an inner hole near the middle small enough to insert a needle, as for pricking, and may it be of tin, with a wick in front so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and let there be one in the middle a crossbar of tin or iron to put a candle holder into, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of adults, and of thin people from those of fat people.
