Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup on the limb: take the candle of wax or resin, and put it into the suction cup through the crossbar that is in the suction cup, so that the flame is at the bottom of the suction cup to avoid burning the patient; then put it on the limb, and let your two fingers be above the hole as we have said, so that when you wish, the vapor goes out, and remove the suction cup; and around the hole place the resin as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the application of the suction cup for diseases of the pleura, in any acute condition, it has no needle or perforation, and is applied with force only when it is filled with fluid, and placed on the limb solely; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Suction cups are applied with force only to areas where it is impossible to place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in exposed flesh, such as that of a dove or swan, and others like them; and the quality of the suction must be such that when you find blisters in clear, sweet water without corruption, you take them; and place one nut in sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing inside; then bleed by vein and suction, afterwards rub the limb until it is red, and put on the blisters; and when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a suction cup can be placed, then apply it, for this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not so, lift the shoulder blade, and then with water, very well, and then drain it; and if the shoulder heals too late after the course of the veins, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place on it until the flesh is infected; and if there are many wounds, place on it broken vitriol or gallstones, and similar things, until they are infected; or you may put over the shoulder half of peeled peas, and let them remain until they dry out at the shoulder, to stop bleeding now; and if you have more need of this, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins do not wish to take, rub the shoulder with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until the vein gives, and then place it on; as soon as they smell the blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they are ready, powder a little aloes and ground salt or ashes over them, and they will stop bleeding now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the knowledge contained in this chapter did not appear in any of the ancient books or letters anyone read; and for this reason, the science has been excluded from our land, for I found no good use for it. I know nothing of it except through the science of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I treated it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life. And I have described here what is contained, summarized at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the summary of the word and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twists or sprain comes to any person, it is necessary to hasten to heal the patient on both sides, if nothing else affects him, such as bodily weakness, or illness, or old age; or if his tendons are not very tight, or too cold; and he should consume cold herbs, that is to say cold jujubes, and meat of fowl and chervil, and not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or spreading of matter in the limb; then the patient returns to his former governance as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with meats that promote good healing or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, lentils, beef liver, oysters, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And in good healing, the flesh regrows more quickly and the fractures heal faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones in the old and decrepit cannot heal or join well according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone and apply large bandages which will firm up and unite the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not completely restrict its movement, for this reason it is necessary to nourish with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go round, and others that are jagged, like the cuts of a writing pen.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is fracture with wound, and fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own method and proper tool for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place; and fractures of the bone are known by the deformity of the limb, and clearly by displacement, and a tapping with the hand; and when there is no deformation, nor pain on touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there may be no fracture; but it can well have deformation, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it by hand, but place medicines that follow here, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in length, and are the two parts disjoined, you must now put them back equally, as if abscesses were covered and came to life; and if abscesses hot come, let it remain for a day, until the abscesses be pacified; then set them equally upon the place where you can gently and safely fix them, and know that the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold them as it suits hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, extend them on both sides, whether it is a hand or foot, by your hand if it is a small limb, by two strings, or one string and your hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you must reduce them with all means at the place where you can fix them, and keep in mind that through your work no injury or pain come to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if it seems not quite right: dress it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring about hot abscess and contraction to the limb through their work, as we have often desired.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at point, well chastise the patient so he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and see to it that the limb be so secured that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at point, and it must be put in proper disposition so that no pain is felt; and see to it that it be placed correctly, so that no twists remain when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I have said.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For those with small members, such as wrists and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in soft, fine linen cloths; and for the larger members, such as the thigh and leg, they should be wrapped in a wide and firm bandage, because the large bandages embrace the entire limb and restrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no gap; then tie around with light stoppers, three or four times according to the member, and gently tighten your hand on each bandage, then go above the break and restrain less, as the break can be moved a bit away from it; and gradually soften the bandage, until you perceive a large part of the healthy tissue, then take the other bandage, and wrap again around the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and restrain moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first hour above; then place stoppers of linen or cloth evenly between the tied bandages, making them all equal, then tie everything over the bandage, and put your well-made pads on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put a thing that calms the abscess and reduces swelling on it, and leave it for several days; then remove it with your needles, which should be half as wide as a thick cane, or of wood used to make nails, or from palm fronds, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the needles which one puts on the break are a bit thicker and wider than the others; and should be as long as necessary for the size or length of the limb. Then hold the needles in place just as you did at the first application, then tie a suitable thread over them, just as you did at the first treatment. Closer is tighter, further away less so; and it must be that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax. For if the thread is thick, like I have seen in works done with leaves that make their rounds from twisted linen threads, and this is a great error, because the thread cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not suit that there be less than two fingers' breadth between each needle.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the shoulders of the stakes after the grip in their sound limbs, place over them linen stoppers or bandages of wool, so that it does not swell.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the cauterizer, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to grip all the broken limbs with stakes on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to place strong stakes on them on the first day; rather, do this after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of a hot abscess occurring. And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that stays on the walls of the mill, mix it with abundant egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is a common method for using restorative plasters to treat fractures in various situations, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 ounces of bear's grease and honey and oil of roses and gum arabic and myrrh, 10 drops; frankincense and aloes, 5 drops; and make it into powder, and mix with honey from an egg; if the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for treating twists: take myrrh and visvalia, 10 drops; frankincense and aloes, 9 drops; acacia, 6 drops; armenian bark, 10 drops, and grind well, and mix with water or honey from an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for plastering joints and the bones that are out of place from their sockets, and to soothe the pain that follows, and the cutting of the bone, and the breaking: take new wool, and the fat in oil cooked, and put on the skin.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not cure, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for plastering to cure broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for plastering to restore the break in the bone and to reduce the swelling of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of visvalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches; from each, take one part; grind them and make a paste with wine. If the members are heated, make the paste with moist coriander water or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of plastering stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes during the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visvalve, and seeds of flax, balsam, chamomile, and sarsaparilla, and flowers of violets and chamomile; from each, take one part; grind them and make a paste with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iphyscras states in his book that one should not place anything on the broken limb to restore strength that cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says it should be between too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should place on the broken limb things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster remedy for injury and pain: take mithah and ombrage leaves, or bird feathers, and vismale, and salt equally, and grind them, and make a plaster with them.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it after some time, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if he does not feel pain in this area, do not remove it by hand. And if pain comes to this area, or itching without rest or swelling, you must hasten, and remove it, and take off the plaster now. And use a light cloth, and a moist sponge of sea water, and dip it in water, and lift the limb until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and tie it with a bandage, until you are sure of the warm abscess. And subdue the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle wound care, and a little plaster, but do not bind so tightly as before; and continue this subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is drained and redness and pain and swelling are gone from all of it, and you need to apply a plaster and a bandage, then renew them as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, and it is not dislocated after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes let it remain for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture dries up, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh above; then restrain it more than at first, and let it grow its flesh, as I said before; and if you see the place dry more than is needed, know that nourishment cannot come; apply a piece of hot cloth each time you dislocate it, and let it be every third day, and slightly loosen the bandage; by this work therefore, cut the nourishment to the member, and quickly mend what the foolish menders leave tortmented: it is bad, and such works are fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are, and various shapes, and the causes are predetermined; for there are fractures made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone down to the sypha which is beneath the bone, just as a hatchet or fust does; and because of this, this kind of fracture is called "hatchet fracture.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and it includes both large and small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compression fracture, or a crack from stone, or falling on stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture close to the tissue beneath the bone, or on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as finely as hairs, and is a small crack, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or some similar thing, and causes a piece of bone to enter below, and makes the eyes so as blacksmiths do when they strike on cauldrons; so the stones enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or have had moist bones, such as children's bones; and it happens in all these kinds of fracture where small pieces are dislodged like splinters; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all manners of breaks through their subtraction, and through the inquiry of tests, and through the corrupt flesh that is there.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is discerned by this: when the bone is uncovered and one rubs over it, black breaks appear.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient's symptoms. If you see any bad symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, paralysis, or fever, and if the eyes become突出和红肿, and other similar things due to various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any terrifying symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractures first come to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone rots, and the accidents as we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches to the tissue that covers the brain, you must split the fractured part in such a way: and you must probe the head of the injured person, and uncover above the bone in all ways you can, and more over the figure of the wound. And if bleeding occurs upon uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, aid as necessary, and it is that you fill the head with moistened linen soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses subside, and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin under the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut before with a narrow blade, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then one cuts a larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that one has several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron needle; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it must be pierced through, as one administers incisions with tenons, not perfectly but in such a way that they do not penetrate beyond the bone at the top. Above the point, there should be a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have tenons for all tops. And this is the form of the three kinds of tenons:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone are that you place the needle on the bone, turn to your two sides until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the needle a little bit to another part, and do this throughout, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertsu [a type of surgical tool], and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pinchers; and guard that you do not touch the brain nor the syface.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the delay which has remained of the bone to all other similar instruments, but it must be more tense and more subtle than the other incisors; and if there remains any small bones or no scales, you must remove them gently with the instruments; then cure the wound with cloths and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galien said, which is safer; and it is strong, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is open and moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this incisor a lens-like object, of which its form is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the broken part be on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently tap the bone all around, and take great care of the membrane beneath; if it is rough against the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed too easily and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then you must treat under that roughness, and remove scales with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, in order to administer in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use large razors first and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small incisions and fine breaks, you must administer care according to its need; and this is a matter that is not left to one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the side is uncovered, it must be that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and apply oil of rosemary, placing it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth twice or three times over, with oil of wine and rosemary, placing it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can so as not to burden the side, then cover it with a bandage from above, and do not bind it too tightly that it presses on the wound only; and leave it for one or two days, until the abscesses are calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vermillion, incense powder, and aromatic substances; and make a powder from these things and apply it to the wound, and continue administering bandages without causing irritation; and see that the wound remains clean, not leaving the ointment out nor allowing it to assemble bowen, for when bowen assembles on the brain cloth, it will flow and harm, bringing great mischief to the patient; for when anything biting is placed on the side, nerves will be inflamed above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness does not come forth only because of the medicine we have put on, that it has some virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue one cloth, and put it on the sore; then cure it in the manner of cures that it should be healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts above the neck are broken, or only one of them, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and neither breaks nor causes pain by bowing or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must set your little finger or the thumb from birth, and place the break equally within your index finger, and the knuckle pouch by opening, so that the bone heals according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the thumb and your finger cannot reach the place, you must put it equally on the head of a needle about as large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is on both sides, do the same for the other side, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then place a needle at the thumb's head with linen thread, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you place the other from another side, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the pores of the navel.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer said that we should moisten the tents with butter and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me to be well done, but the tents should be moistened with a preparation of egg white and powder of mill flour. Then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we use goose feathers in lieu of tents, and wrap the area with a bandage, and if the fracture remains, blow on it with the patient. Do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses arise in the nose while you are working on it, you should apply a poultice or wet cloth in rose oil, or with a little dyakin.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not arise in the nose, apply an ointment externally, made of silk powder and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk. Then place it with light stoppers, and do not bind the nose; and if the break in the nose is small, and broken into small pieces, extract it with instruments suitable for this, then stitch the wound, treating things that affect flesh and healing, as ointments and remedies suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with cotton, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is ruptured but there is no wound visible, and the fracture is open only, not broken into pieces but rather like hinges inside, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part of the jaw, you should place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, you should place your right hand's index finger on the fracture gently, and complete it with the other hand by making an opening.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, it is necessary to apply an extension to both parts equally.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs or a rupture, strain them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place on the broken jaw a poultice, and place over it a double layer; and place over this a large well-made pad, or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it securely around the mouth as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the swelling changes, release it on the third day, and then reposition what has changed; and apply a poultice with flour from the mill mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour after you have removed the poultice; and place over the poultice light cloth, and if the poultice dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses remain, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, note if any piece of the bone has been removed; so subtle that it can be extracted with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, close the wound if it is large, and apply suitable poultices to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	by force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful break happens many times in front of the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: either it is broken and separated into two parts, and has pieces, which is the most轻微的复位；或者其中有断裂伴有伤口。
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the break has no wound, that you have two assistants, so that one feels the injured part where the forceful break occurred; and the other extends the neck towards the affected area. Then place the break equally between your two hands, so that the form be as it should, and there be neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round pad of cloth or wool under the shoulder of the patient, and make it as large as necessary; then gently stretch the affected area, and hold the pad with your hand, so that you can place the break equally, as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder downward, because it comes from below, then it is necessary that the patient lie often on his side, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder, and make the attendants support the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then treat the break carefully. If you find pieces detached, you must cut them out; and pull the pieces gently. And if the bone cannot join for any protrusion, use one of your forceps; but place this instrument over the shoulder to prevent leakage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not misplaced, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you can see, with one broad and the other narrow, similar to the wound you made when treating the bones. And when you are certain of a hot abscess, drain the wound, but if the opening is small or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if blisters appear when it comes, soak them in rose oil and vinegar, and apply.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is felt by wounds and by cuts, is that you put over the bone the poultice of flour powder and egg yolk, and place light stops above, and put a sphere underneath if needed; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put the folded cloth over the stops and the poultice; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage hang down; and place the stick on the splint, and turn the bandage up to the neck, under the sphere and under the healthy side; and tighten each part, and when you see that the ties hold the splint properly, and clearly see that the stick does not move over the broken bone, then reward each day, and when the stitches loosen, release them; and have the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow under the sphere to lift the helper up; so it will lighten the injury from the shoulder by the support of the shoulder, or you tie the arm at the neck, and do not untie it until bad accidents occur, until twenty days; then reapply the poultice if needed, and keep it tight and let it be thus until it is restored; and it is fully restored in twenty-eight days, and in less time for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	that often happens when the shoulder breaks or is wide off at either end, and cannot be moved except by touch; arrange the parts according to the figure of the break, and reset them according to their natural form in all ways that you can; then put over the limb powder of flour with abundant egg, and light stops, and place a double flag above; then place a large and subtle strip, slightly wider than the shoulder, and where there are movements anywhere in the shoulder, fill those areas with linen stops so that the strip stays even; and then tightly wrap it with a large bandage, so that the strip does not move from its place, and check the ligature each day; whenever it loosens, rewrap it, and adjust the strip if it is out of place, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty or二十五天，或者二十五天。当这些数字完成时，解开绷带，确保无误，因为骨头不能轻易复位。
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone tents out and is not over the heart, incise it, remove the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the strong ligament to cool the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is often broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it breaks frequently at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines outward, and the patient feels great pain, along with swelling. Immediately, and by accident, they may vomit blood, and the movements in the broken bones become apparent, and everyone can see this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies mostly on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join the ribs together with your hands, placing them in perfect alignment as you can. Then apply plasters and ointments over the fine saline or light bandage, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it tightly to the broken bone so it does not move; turn the knot roundly on the back and adjust it suitably, tightening it every hour. If it gets loose, tighten it again. And if it needs to be untied for corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, you must act quickly, untie it, remove the plaster, and treat the area as in other treatments; then reapply the plaster and bandage until it heals fully.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaking of the ribs comes from force only behind the shoulders and at the top within, and they bend due to being slippery; and one feels it well in the examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you align the break as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is turning inward, the patient feels great pain and prickling, similar to tears, because the bone punctures the membrane; they writhe in pain, and immediately vomit much blood, which is a serious health issue. The ancients used great skill to treat this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say it is necessary to give foods that swell the belly to counteract the heat.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make such incisions into abscesses that there should not be pus if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if pus has come, then drain it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that we should apply suction cups to the shoulder to draw out the poison strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the suction cup will draw out the excess toxins due to the weakness of the condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that we should cover the shoulder with wetted wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to equalize the treatment inside, then it should be treated with a pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because the bone touches the membrane, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to incise above the rib of the broken side, and it is necessary to place something under the instrument to protect the heart; and then one must cut the bone, and draw lightly, and then suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses continue to come, put moist cloths in rose oil on the rib; and place it on the side where it should be. Cure while observing the side for what is needed for the abscess, and let him lie on his side where it needs to be until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Any time the bones of the neck break, and often it bends; and similarly with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, observe whether their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when pricked with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many respects, and if they can move and feel well when pricked with a needle, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and the patient will recover if proper treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is healed or not, see if the flesh is softened, and if the accidents are in the hands, and on the back with windiness and effortless evacuation; and when one has soothed it on their abdomen, there is effortless evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it has been soothed on their back and they wish to sit up, they cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if it does not labor at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not come to them, it is the matter less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply oil of roses or oil of egg yolk if there is a hot abscess. Then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage. Instruct the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel pain until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone separates, it is necessary to cover over the heart; remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if large, with one suture, then treat with ointment promoting flesh growth until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," you must take your left hand's fist and place it evenly in your right hand at your power, then apply the plaster and bandage over it, if you need them; then bind it. If there are separated bones, cut out, remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Often it happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there will be but a slight alleviation in the head; stretch long, and decline to the side, and pain comes to the patient at the site, swelling, and redness where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the brace; and know which is the break and its figure; and if the break is only at the head, set it equal to that break, so that it be in natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, you make the patient lie on his stomach so that the restoration of that break may be aligned.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it equal, apply a plaster, then place a stick or a rod over it, and bind the brace so that it does not move. And fill the area under the ribs, so that the binding is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his sound side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses are hot and come, do not touch them until the abscesses are appeased, and apply what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold them as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires are those between the scapula and the head of the shoulder. And if they are dislocated, you must restore them according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a stick of medium size, as follows:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with two ligatures, and draw them up, and seat the patient on the seat; then place his broken arm on the post, until it comes to the axilla, and have in the middle a piece of wood, then hang on any heavy thing or let the attendants extend downwards; then put the reaper's blade equal to his hands together, so that the broken part returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his stretcher, and binds his hand to his neck, then commands two attendants that one hold what is on the reaper's blade at his hands, and the other hold below the ligature, extending each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligature both below and above the reaper's blade, and extend each attendant to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it must be that you place the middle line over the axilla, and the other towards the cut, under the break; and also if the break is opposite the cut, it must be placed lightly, without labor, so that the break is equal over the bone, and over the cut; then set the break evenly as it should be, and bind it, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, you must not bind it tightly for seven days, and place moistened wool in lint and rose oil until the abscesses are pacified; then bind it, and the way to bind it is that you put the plaster over the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder support, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the bandage, binding over the shoulder support and over the arm, so that the arm is in a sling, unless anything prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stakes, and place one wider and stronger stake above the fracture, with two fingers' width between each stake, and let each stake be so large that it passes the fracture by three fingers on each side; then pull on the stakes as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less by pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stakes and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you set the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it free for seven days, as we have said; then look at each three days the healing, to ensure pruritus does not swell or arise at the place, or the granulations cannot come to the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come to pass, let the dislocation not be undone after three days or more, and let the patient lie on his back, and keep his hands over his stomach; place under the shoulder a cushion filled with evenly sized wool, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, nor become soft the ligaments; by the virtue of medicine, it will heal, and let him eat the meat we have placed before, in such a manner that the meat be at first finely chopped; and when it begins to take, let it be generous.
